<Author>debby1986
<Content>Gone with the Wind This year has been very difficult and we needed a place to relax and enjoy each other. The LePavillon Hotel was exactly what we needed. If you have seen the movie Gone w/the Wind then the lobby will be a replica. Of course this is just my opinion. The lobby and the dining room was exquisite. Now I must confess that the room (King size) how ever breathtaking it was, is a little small but still very beautiful. The decor of the bathroom was chic. But you won't be in the room that much because there is so much to do. We were there for five days. Most of the time we rode the street car which is a 1.25 one way. I would also recommend that if you are going to be out pretty late take the taxi from LePavillion to the casino or to the French Quarter. It will run you around $8 or $9 dollars one way. I probably gained 10lbs because food is everywhere. The hotel offers a buffet for $18 have Pat make you an omelet!!!!. Often we would return to the hotel late and would still be hungry. The food from room service was great. It will probably run you around $50 and up. Also, please, please take the Katina tour. What you see in the tourist area is not what you will see during this tour. If while you are on the tour and they don't mention about the bridge that goes to Ward 9, please inquire. Overall we are looking to revisit the LePavillon in April. Oh, I must also tell you don't remove anything from the Refreshment Center unless you are going to pay for it. The refreshment center has a sensor and records everything you remove. I found out the hard way, but they removed it from my bill. I truly enjoyed myself and I can't wait until April (my birthday).  
<Date>Dec 17, 2008

<Author>LY776
<Content>A Grand Old Hotel In The Big Easy This is a grand hotel with tons of character. A beautiful lobby that looks like it came out of a movie set. Gaudy and over the top, just like something in New Orleans should be.The service was warm without being pushy. Particularly the staff in the Crystal Room Dining Room was particularly pleasant. I had booked on Orbitz and there was a free breakfast buffet included. This was without a doubt the most beautiful breakfast room I have ever eaten in (and I have stayed in a few nice hotels around the world). If I had not had included for free, I am not sure I would have shelled out 17.99 for the breakfast as I don't eat that much. However, the spread was impressive and a great brunch deal for those with an appetite. And unlike the other Orbitz customer who felt they had received a worse room due to this breakfast deal, I was actually given an upgrade for my room.The room itself was well appointed and quiet. The style is Victorian with tall and spacious rooms. Admittedly, this is a 100 year old hotel and not everything is brand spanking new. The bathtub and shower could use a wee bit of an upgrade. But certainly nothing was wrong enough that should put off anyone. The 37 or so pillows on the bed were probably more than I need, but that is the kind of over the top decoration choices that give the hotel its particular charm. I admit I also like a hotel that still gives you personalized terry cloth robes to use, has their own stationery in the rooms, and leaves you a welcome note in an engraved card. The hotel is in walking distance to the French Quarter. There are also some interesting neighborhoods just across the street around the courthouse and other legal buildings and alleys. Sadly, like most of New Orleans in the area you can find many buildings and businesses still waiting to recover from Katrina. Not everything in the hotel was perfect, and any hundred year old hotel has a few frayed edges. At the same time, there are wonderful ornate hallways and public spaces that you rarely find outside of hotels costing many times more. If you want austere, sterile, perfection, you probably are better going with some chic uber modern chain (and probably the New Orleans Big Easy attitude isn't going to be for you anyway). If you want something unique that seems to fit the mood of New Orleans in a grand (but not stuffy) manner - then you're going to like your stay at Le Pavillon.  
<Date>Dec 14, 2008

<Content>Pretty lobby, but... I'll start off by saying that I got a great deal on Orbitz that included the breakfast buffet which is valued at $18pp. The food and service was great. The location is great, close enough and far enough from the French Quarter. We had a great rate, and that's what makes my review above average.

<Author>martypaula
<Content>Top Notch We booked via Hotwire for $78 per night. We were very happy to see the location. We were in town for Tulane Parent's weekend, so the location was central to campus, french quarter, and Magazine Street. Upon arrival, we were swiftly brought in to check in. We were taken to our room by Nabeel ,who was respectful (ladies first on the elevator), informative about the history of the hotel, and just plain friendly. For the next few days, he greeted us by name every time we walked through the lobby. We had limited time for a quick lunch and he quickly pointed us to a local spot called PG just a block away. It was a great reasonable eatery with local specials..crab cakes, jambalaya, shrimp creole. My husband went for breakfast as well . Nabeel should be commended for his representation of this hotel. It is evident that he loves this jewel in the city. Every staff member we encountered during our stay were polite and friendly. One of my favorite things about New Orleans in general is how hard they ty to make you feel welcome. True southern hospitality!The room was small, but adequate. The bathroom small as well. It was very clean and stocked with nice toiletries. When in New Orleans, I don't expect to spend a lot of time in the room, so no complaints. I found the room to be quite sound proof. Hot chocolate (delicious) and peanut butter sandwiches served each evening in the lobby were yummy. Le Pavillon tradition.Although parking was expensive, 28.00 plus about 3.00 tax, Le Pavillon is one of the few upscale hotels that offers free in room wireless internet. I have paid fifteen or more per laptop at other New Orleans Hotels, as well exorbitant parking fees..I would definately stay at this hotel again.A few suggestions for management.....I would love a coffee maker in the room. or complimentary coffee in the lobbyMany of the other upscale hotels offer cold beverages in the lobby late afternoon (lemonade or fruit flavored water), especially refeshing for dehydrated guests.Overall, a great stay!

<Author>faithd58
<Content>Firm 4 star hotel We stayed here for four nights July 31-August 4. The hotel is beautiful. It definitely evokes the old world French feeling that one is looking for when staying in New Orleans. Housekeeping was wonderful. Food was a bit pricey when eating at the hotel restaurants and would be described as usual hotel fare.Check in and out were great. We received the local paper daily and USA Today while staying.We had a few small glitches with the plumbing in the bathroom...the water wouldn't turn off every time...we did not report this tho as we usually were able to turn it off. The beds, although beautiful were really not that comfortable...it would behoove the hotel to bump it up on the linens (sheets, pillowcases) and perhaps check out the mattresses.Also, usually in 5* hotels, the management will contact the guest to inquire regarding the room status and to insure all is well after check in. It's a small but important detail.The bartender (I think her name is Gretchen) was very friendly. There was a piano player in the bar on Friday night and he was very good and friendly.The staff were courteous, helpful and pleasant. I was disappointed at times with little things...empty water bottles laying on the ground by the jacuzzi, milk carton left on the outside steps overnight by some guest after the pb j treat which is offered by the hotel gratis. The PB  J treat in the evenings was great. The hot chocolate was excellent.We had originally rented a car and the cost to park at the hotel overnight is 28.00 per night, which is exorbitant and should be reconsidered for hotel guests.When we were leaving, we requested a cab. The bell hop whistled and the cabbie pulled up. His van was disgustingly dirty. The hotel should check this out. Although it wasn't a part of our stay, it was the finish and although it is a cab, the hotel should only solicit those cabbies who provide good, clean service (cabbies generally sit right outside of the hotel)Overall, I would stay here again. We had a wonderful time. The hotel needs to only focus on these few small details in order to be a true 5*.

<Author>craldiri
<Content>Beautiful Exterior...But What Lies Beneath Hotel is in a good location, has a great deal of classic decor and charm and some staff are courteous. When I arrived ready to unload bags and passengers I was initially annoyed by the doorman who wanted me to somehow park further to the right than was physically possible. Recommendation - Doorman should be extra courteous and understanding to make up for a very small driveway. He ultimately amended himself. Parking fee seemed high at over $30 for one night as compared to a recent trip to Northern California staying at the Renaissance. The registration area also seems small as compared to other hotels and is further obscured by a huge plant separating the two work stations. I almost missed it walking into the hotel. Somehow their registration system had me down for two nights, when I had booked only one night. Desk person was beginning to argue how many nights I had checked in until I showed her the printed receipt clearly pointing out one night. This was the second bad impression, but she too also regulated herself and we concluded the business at hand. The young bellman who helped us to the room with our bags made a very positive impression. He was well-spoken, courteous, not overly intrusive with questions. Even when he offered to orient us to our room (something I never accept), I said ok. Main difficulty was that the room we stayed in (609) is very dusty, dark and smells of mold and mildew. Positively cavelike. Bath had visible signs of mold. In fact the entire 6th floor smells musty. This gives the impression of lack of care and led me to wonder whether there might be health risks in ordering food or using the hotel's other amenities like the pool. Concierge gave us some good ideas for a family friendly dinner. PBJ reception is the first I ever attended and it is a nice idea, unfortunately executed poorly. Hot chocolate was finished by the time daughter and I got there. Lack of more than one serving station meant everyone had to line up which made this nice idea a chore. Recommendation - Multiple serving stations that are staggered throughout the lobby so that only minimal lines are formed. The lack of adequate numbers of staff when checking out made it take longer than it needed to and required lining up or waiting when the only person on duty managing the desk needed to also check someone's baggage. Thankfully there was a quick checkout option. This is a beautiful historic hotel that could be great with a bit more investment in the infrastructure, staff training and better overall management.

<Author>Terry9
<Content>A Hotel to Remember A lot of nice hotels in New Orleans seem to still be at get-tourists-here prices, but our stay at Le Pavillon seemed like a steal for the Hotwire price of $74 a night. Except for one edgy desk person (we won't hold that against the hotel), the staff exudes service. The hotel's location wasn't as close to the French Quarter as we would have liked, but the concierge gave us great advice on where and when it's safest to walk there (which we enjoyed).The hotel is beautiful, not only in the amazing lobby, but also in the rooms. I've never seen such a beautiful sink in a hotel room! The beds were high end comfort and bathroom amenities were top of the line. We did miss the in-room coffee maker that the other hotels we stayed at provided, but we found free bottled water available in the fitness room. The roof top pool was pretty, but small and cold, but the view was worth going up for. Of course, not to be missed, is PBJ hour. It was worth keeping our kids up for. We decided peanut butter and jelly sandwiches and hot cocoa never tasted so good!

<Author>jack78Raleigh
<Content>Great Hotel and Great City My stay at Le Pavillon could not have been any better. When you enter the hotel lobby, it is immediately evident a great deal of love and care has gone into maintaining this beautiful and historic hotel. I can imagine this hotel probably looks as good or better now than it did when it opened over 100 years ago. This attention to detail carries over to the guest rooms. The suite we stayed in was imaculately maintained with beautiful antiques throughout.Perhaps more impressive than the building was the hotel staff. Often hotels of this caliber can be stuffy and pretentious. Not Le Pavillon. I have never felt so welcome and at home in a hotel before in my life! Le Pavillon captures the essence of what makes New Orleans such a special city (the people and culture). Make sure you have breakfast in the Crystal Room and let Ms. Pat make you a special omlet. She is unforgetable.By the way, New Orleans is definitely getting back in the swing of things. The streets in the French Quarter are extremely clean and the food is better than ever.

<Author>TravellinwithFamily
<Content>A historic hotel, wonderful staff My husband and I stayed at Le Pavillon for one week in June, while he attended a conference in NOLA. Consistent with other reviewer comments, the first room assigned, was small for the large size furniture it was expected to accommodate and it also needed some TLC. When we mentioned our concerns to front desk staff, they addressed each quickly. We had opportunity to move to a larger room, when another couple checked out, and enjoyed it immensely for the balance of our stay. The staff from the front desk, housekeeping, bar and dining room were impeccable in their service delivery and general friendliness. We enjoyed the roof top pool and hot tub, cabanas, and the late night peanut butter and jelly sandwich tradition at this fine hotel. The elegance of the hotel, coupled with the warmth of the people we met, made for an excellent first trip to NOLA, start to finish. Le Pavillon, and its staff, will remain a wonderful part of our memories of this great City still recovering post Katrina.Tip for the Do it Yourself Traveller: Get a ride all day $5.00 pass for the Transit from Guest Services. Take the St. Charles Streetcar to the Garden District to enjoy the fine homes and universities. Consider getting off at Washington Avenue to visit Lafayette Cemetery, and enjoy a snack or meal at the Camellia Grill or Le Madeline at the end of the line before catching another streetcar back to the hotel. The stop for the St. Charles streetcar is less than a block from Le Pavillon. Enjoy!

<Author>anthropomom
<Content>An Historic Jewel in the Heart of the City! This hotel was built in 1907 and it is located a few blocks away from Canal Street, which separates the old French Quarter area from the other parts of town. You are not in the noisy or rowdy parts of town here, and your accomodations are not strictly as modern as they might be at some of the newer properties, but there is a grace about Le Pavillon that is very appealing, especially if you are a grownup (of any age). Enjoy the Victorian feel of the loby and lounge with its glorious chandeliers; and the late night snacks provided in the lobby.The management and the staff are nothing but courteous and helpful. Some of our fellow visitors said that their room was too small perhaps, but we could not complain as we were upgraded quite grandly from the room we had reserved.My family especially enjoyed the rooftop pool at night. When we were there, we had it almost to ourselves with the exception of another small group with whom we shared some great conversation. It's not a kid's splashy type of situation- again this is an elegant lady of a property, a great value for its location and quietness. Valet parking is standard at Le Pavillon. You will pay a fee for it but parking in New Orleans is going to cost money any-which-way you look.

<Author>asf1950
<Content>Great Deal at $100 Per Night We called the hotel directly and our four-night stay cost us just $450 including all taxes -- and we were upgraded to a deluxe king room. The room was smallish and narrow, and the bathroom could have used a lot more shelf space. Still, everything was clean and dirt-free (except for a few areas which required the moving of furniture), and nicely appointed. Pros: free bottled water, turn-down service, plenty of towels, a good bed, lots of hot water and solid water pressure, shower head high on wall, room-darkening curtains, friendly and competent staff (especially the taxi starters and bell staff).Cons: bottom sheet of bed not fitted, ineffective half-size splash-guard in shower, air conditioner makes loud pops if fan set to auto, bathroom door opens outward (due to sink placement), shower head is non-adjustable, we had to ask for more pillows (only got three), the usual hallway noise/talking and slamming of doors, pricey room service.The hotel is a few blocks from the French Quarter, and we took a lot of streetcars and taxis during our stay to get to other attractions. It's in a business area, which seemed quiet, well-lit and safe, even during a late-night walk back to the hotel. The rooftop pool and jacuzzi were more appealing in the photos. Overall, the place's sparkling appearance belies its age of 100 years. Recommended.

<Author>ChrisIsOnTheRoad
<Content>Charm, Class and History Read the TripAdvisor reviews prior to our visit. Let me see if I can provide some of the clarity I was looking for before our stay. Le Pavillon Hotel is a grand, older hotel. It was built in 1907 and is (do the math) now over 100 years old. In my experience there are both advantages and compromises in staying at such a property. I like my history but I also like my latest and greatest features and technology and I'm generally not a BB guy. Le Pavillon is definitely worth some of the compromises.The location is good if you want to be near the Superdome, Central Business District and French Quarter. The good news if you want it a bit quieter at night is that you are very near but not in the French Quarter. We booked on Hotwire and as other reviewers have suggested upgraded to a Deluxe King room. Room service was excellent and prompt. In general the service was tremendous from every staff member that we encountered. Very attentive. For example as I was ordering a snack one afternoon the phone seemed to keep cutting out. Before the snack even arrived a maintenance person was there to repair the phone.... And we hadn't reported a phone problem. Will definitely stay there again.

<Author>B0bL
<Content>A Special Hotel I鈥檒l start by saying that we loved our stay at Le Pavillon. Then go on to say that this may not be the hotel for everyone. This is not a national chain hotel; it is a place that is so rich in tradition and elegance that some may feel uncomfortable in a place that it is not decorated by Cort Furniture, with gas station art on the walls, lumpy beds and stiff scratchy linens. Le Pavillon is unique. It is beautifully appointed, spotlessly clean and very gracious. The room in which we stayed was very comfortable though could have used a bit more flat surface space. Having read many of the reviews before our stay we were a bit worried about the bedding. We had no reason to. The king sized bed was almost as comfortable as our 5鈥?pillow top. The room was beautiful, the chairs comfortable  the rest of the furniture was quite elegant. The bathroom was incredible. It was entirely modernized with very sexy black tiles and the wall above the countertop was mirrored from backsplash to ceiling. The shower head was a beautiful ceramic 鈥渟quash flower鈥?with plenty of pressure and hot water. Nice bathrobes were provided and there were large towels aplenty. One of the best I鈥檝e seen in my travels.We arrived fairly early in the day and were given an early check in. When we came back in from an hour stroll around the area we found a basket of fruit and a bottle of their own bottled local spring water in the room. While reading the hotel directory I noticed that coffee makers were available by calling guest services. I called and within an hour they delivered a coffee maker, oversized cups and Community Coffee. This was kept stocked for entire stay. After returning from dinner we found our bed turned down, two more bottles of water and two peanut butter and jelly cookies with the recipe on our night table. This was repeated each night.The hotel staff was fantastic. Every request that we made was granted. One of the nights was my wife鈥檚 birthday and she wanted a Muffelatta from Napoleon House but they stop serving food at 5:30 and that was too early for us so I asked the concierge if we could bring one in and have it heated up in their kitchen. 鈥淵es sir just ask the hostess and we鈥檒l take care of it for you鈥?was the answer. When the time came I spoke with the hostess and gave directions on the proper heating of the sandwich which meant wrapped in tinfoil in the oven for twenty to thirty minutes not the microwave. It was done to perfection. On the way back to the room we were the envy of all of the guest that we ran into.The Concierge staff was extremely knowledgeable and helpful. We wanted to visit a cemetery and they recommended a tour with a non profit that is involved with the cemetery rather that a crowded tour operated by one of the big companies. The same kind of recommendation was made for a bayou tour.Our only complaint was there was that the room refrigerator was filled with mini bar items. We prefer our own favorite beverages and foods whilst traveling but when we requested and extra ice bucket one was delivered immediately.All in all a very satisfying stay and we will stay again next year when we return for Jazz Fest.A big thanks to the staff of Le Pavillon

<Author>Didrick
<Content>Doesn't live up to its own opinion of itself We booked two rooms at this hotel for three nights in April, partly based on glowing reports on Tripadvisor. It was our first visit to New Orleans and we knew the hotel was going to be somewhat over the top in terms of presentation and decor.But behind the showy facade there was little to justify the $250 per room per night. The hotel staff mostly weren't able to live up to the expectations presented by the in-house PR team. Some were downright miserable. Yet every morning a note from management was left on the bed, written in peculiarly servile language, explaining how dedicated the staff are to granting peace and rest while under our roof. Cool. So why vacuum the hall outside the room at 8.30am to wake us up? And why fill the room with all those decorative pillows yet provide next to nowhere to put our clothes? And why no tea and coffee making facilities in the room? The note goes on, May every call you make, every message you receive and every person you meet add to your joy. Great. So why try to charge us six times for breakfast we'd prepaid, why charge us for parking a car we didn't have and why insist on using our first names but get them wrong in spite of repeated corrections? If you don't take this place seriously - before you go to bed they serve free jam sandwiches among the vast array of artworks in the lobby for heaven's sake - you'll enjoy this place but no way is it worth the money. And don't believe the hype.

<Author>wisgirl01
<Content>Impeccable service! Just returned from my stay at Le Pavillion, which was wonderful. I visit New Orleans several times a year and have stayed in many different hotels there, this was my second stay at Le Pavillion. I am also a frequent business traveler. While the hotel is in a great location, and doesn't compare to other 4 stars I've stayed in bedding or amenity-wise, the stellar service is what made my experience memorable. Here is why:1. My luggage did not arrive on my flight, and was delivered to the hotel several hours later. While I was in the check-in line, the bellman, Nabil, asked if he could help me. I told him with a smile, No thanks, just checking in, with no luggage. He asked right away if I needed a toothbrush or anything. I said that would be great. He came back a few seconds later with a toothbrush, paste and deoderant. I did not ask for this, he was just attentive and it was very appreciated.2. My luggage came very late that night (230am) and it was wet. The desk attendant asked if there was anything I needed as my bag was wet - again, attention to detail that was not asked for. 3. The next morning was a bit chilly, but I visited the pool anyway. I was the only one there, reading my paper on a chaise. A housekeeper came out to blow leaves off the patio with a blower. I didn't care, she was just doing her job. About 2 minutes into this, someone came out and called her away. She came back and said, I'm so sorry to have disturbed you and began to sweep the leaves up instead of blow them. I told her she did not disturb me, it was fine. But what?? Someone was aware that one guest was out there, so she changed her routine to accomodate. Again, I didn't care or complain about this. 4. When I was leaving my room to check out, a housekeeper had just stepped off the elevator and was going down the hall in the opposite direction. She saw me come out of my room, from quite far away, and went back to the elevator to hold the door for me. 5. When I checked out, there was a mistake on my bill from the service bar that I did not even know about. The desk agent, who was training asked if I had anything from the service bar. I told her what I had, she said, well this is an error then, I will adjust your bill and she credited me $56. Once again, unsolicited. I was truly amazed by the level of service exhibited by every single person I encountered during this stay. While the rooms are not the newest, or the beds the best, and there was no coffee maker in the room - that is not what will stand out in my mind. The excellent service and attitude of the employees is what made this stay most enjoyable. I would have no hesitation to return or recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>katamie
<Content>The Best! Le Pavillon was a great stay from start to finish. The hotel itself is grand - the lobby is like walking into a French Palace with the beautiful chandeliers and antique furniture. The staff of the hotel were so friendly and helpful - every single one that you passed in the hallway would say hello and perhaps ask about your stay. We did not get one of the premium rooms, but the one we had was more than enough. It was large, it had beautiful furniture, a fridge, a safe, and although the bathroom was not huge, it was very nice with adequate room. The Crystal Room had fabulous Breakfast and Lunch Buffets, and the Bar menu and room service menu were also great. The Peanut Butter Sandwich tradition in the evenings was so much fun! Although we didn't use the rooftop pool and spa, I would make sure to make sue of them the next time! The hotel is a few blocks outside the French Quarter but close enough that walking to the Quarter is not an issue, and it doesn't hurt to burn a few extra calories after eating all that great food! I accidentally left a pair of pants when we checked out. When I contacted the hotel, they did in fact have them and they were terrific about getting them shipped back to me.

<Author>Tarheel21
<Content>OK hotel but not great I booked this hotel based on the reviews on this website at the time I was looking to make a reservation. My husband and I are here for a conference without the kids so we wanted a nice place to stay. I've been screwed before staying at hotels where the conferences are hosted so we were looking for something different. When I booked on this website, this hotel was ranked #1 of all the hotels in NOLA. Well, now I know the #1 was way over the top. The hotel is historic but I think that must mean shabby. The paint in our room is peeling, the A/C is REALLY loud and the toilets don't flush very well. The worst part is the bed - it is really old and worn out. The hotel website says the bed has luxury linens but that is a gross exaggeration. These linens are exactly like every other hotel I've ever stayed in. I consider the linens at the Ritz to be luxury and these are nothing like that. There are no fitted sheets and every time my husband turns over, the sheets come off the bed on his side and get all lumpy. The pillows are as bad as a previous poster said. We called down over an hour ago for new pillows but no one has shown up with them yet. The staff is sort of friendly but nothing like what has been described in prior posts. I don't see anyone going out of their way to assist us. The hotel is in a nice location - right between the Riverwalk and just far enough out of the French Quarter to get away from all the drunks when you've had enough. Overall, a very average hotel with a few unique historic touches.

<Author>Crescentcityfan
<Content>A brilliant hotel in every respect This hotel has real old-fashioned New Orleans charm with its oil paintings and antiques. The hotel overall was very nice and just the right distance away from the French Quarter but what made our stay really special was the service and the staff, particulary the staff in the dining room at breakfast and the porters. The service they offer is not only better than in any other 4 or 5 star hotel I have stayed at (and I have stayed at quite a few!) but they are so charming and friendly you leave the hotel each day with a big smile on your face - I was hoping for some of the famous Southern hospitality and I definitely got it at this hotel! I can definitely recommend the Hurricaine cocktail made by the nice German bartender lady (better than the one I had at Pat OBrien's!) and Miss Pettie's Bananas Foster waffles were absolutely devine! What a charming, delightful hotel - it certainly contributed towards a very good first impression of New Orleans. I would highly recommend New Orleans and this hotel to anybody. What a contrast to the sea of miserable faces I was greeted with when I arrived back in London!

<Author>HopSkipJump
<Content>I love this hotel There's some bad but overall, it's great. First, the bad:1. Ok, it's me. I'll admit it. I'm very picky about pillows. I can't stand skinny hotel pillows and even though there were a lot of them -- and some of them were quite LONG, they were all really flat. I tried stacking them or folding them in half but they wouldn't stay put and I thought all was lost until I decided to take one out of its pillow case, fold it in half width-wise and put it back in the case. Problem solved! Since it was such a LONG pillow to begin with, it ended up half as long but still long enough.2. This hotel is in the central business district, 4 blocks from the edge of the French Quarter. It takes about 15 minutes to walk to the center of the French Quarter or a few minutes by taxi or by street car. This did not bother us at all but if you want to be able to stumble out of a bar and into your hotel, this isn't the place for you. If you do walk, go south on Poydras (in front of the hotel) and then turn left to get to the French Quarter. If you do the opposite (go east, along the side of the hotel and then turn south to enter the Quarter), it takes longer since the streets are not in a perfect grid, there. It's also a prettier walk down Poydras than the other way,Now, the good...1. The hotel is beautiful. The front of the building is much nicer than it looks on the website and the lobby is gorgeous as is the dining room (including its large fireplace) and bar area.2, The room was large and beautifully furnished. (A previous poster said the room was small?!). There was room for 2 queen beds plus a desk on one side and a round table with 2 large arm chairs on the other. That's big enough, isn't it? The bath had been remodeled and the shower was taller than me at 6'3 (1.9 m).3. The night-time peanut butter and jelly buffet with hot cocoa was great fun.4. There was free, 24-hour internet access via a PC on the second floor (for those of us who don't like dragging our lap tops with us). Ask for the password at the front desk.5. EVERYONE who worked there was incredibly kind and thoughtful. We were given great recommendations for a jazz club as well as a place for pecan pie.6. The rooftop pool is on the small size but New Orleans is not really a resort city so we weren't put off by it. We did relax and talk on 2 chaise lounges, that are away from the pool in a little cabana, one late afternoon for about 2 hours and watched the sky get dark.7. We got the room on Hotwire for $90-something and it was a great value.

<Author>superjacques
<Content>Better Choices Available I am a native New Orleanian and at the time was living about 100 miles away and traveling back and forth for business and leisure weekly. I routinely stay at the Omni Royal Orleans as well as the Sheraton on Canal Street for the same approximate price and have found the staff to be much more friendly at those hotels than at Le Pavilion. The rooms can be very small, minibar ridiculously expensive (even for New Orleans), and the parking very high. Also, I happened to stay the last time during some event and had to wear a wristband to get to my room like I was a kid on spring break. Very obnoxious. I cut it off because I could not sleep with it on and they charged me $35 for another one in the morning after I was refused access to the elevator to my room! Not a terrible hotel, quite beautiful lobby and close to the Superdome but there are much better choices available in the French Quarter.

<Content>There's no place like home...unless it's Le Pavillon!!! As a business traveler who spends up to 40 weekends a year in different hotels throughout the country, and occasionally a few other countries, I tend to become overly picky by the end of my stays. There's no place like home after all, unless it's Le Pavillon Hotel it turns out! I have never seen such a well-preserved and well-maintained historical hotel, though The Emily Morgan in San Antonio and The Jerome in Aspen do their best. Never have I felt so at home while feeling so pampered while traveling for work or pleasure. Since I do both in New Orleans as often as possible I promise myself to always do whatever I can to stay at Le Pavillon!

<Author>davine1
<Content>Incredibly Disappointing I'm a native of N.O. and as a child, I marveled at the beauty of LePavilion, hoping one day I'd would stay there. Coming back to N.O. for the Christmas holiday, I decided that my husband, daughter and I should book a stay in a nice, upscale N.O. hotel. LePavilion fit the bill, and Priceline offered a price that made it easy. Unfortunately, the stay was incredibly disappointing. With this hotel, I learned that historic essentially means old. While nicely decorated, the standard room we booked was as small as a matchbox. The bathroom was so small that my husband and I could not stand in it at the same time. Additionally, the fan in the bathroom sounded like a motorbike, the fixtures were rusted and there was hardly any room on the counter. The bed only had 2 pillows and the sheets weren't fitted. Two suitcases barely fit in the closet and the bed was only about 2 feet from the entertainment console/chest, making it difficult to walk around the bed. We needed a microwave for the room and when they brought it, there was only one extra outlet in and the microwave cord was too short to reach it. So, we had to use space on the writing desk, which took up more needed room.We were anxious to have the advertised $17.99 Sunday brunch, only to find out after we ate that on Saints Sundays the same $17.99 buffet is $35.00 per person. And while I've been to many brunch buffets in many nice places, the waffle station was the only thing worth mentioning. Everything else was beautifully displayed, the environment was nice, but the food was mediocre. The staff was very friendly and attentive. That was the only truly pleasant experience we had there. I suppose the upgraded rooms are better, maybe even larger, but for a simple standard room, LePavilion is over-rated, old and in desperate need of a room overhaul. The outside of the hotel and the lobby are beautiful. The standard room fell incredibly short.

<Author>jimshonk
<Content>World Class Service, average room Stayed for the BCS Bowl. Great location, great service, great food, wonderful lobby. When you get into your room though, the physical product is simply not in keeping with luxury tier or branded business competition. They offer two pillows per bed (we had two queen beds), and a basic mattress with an old style hotle bedspread rather than a duvet cover. They must upgrade the bedding standard to meet the standards set by Marriott, Hilton and Hyatt business-class hotels, let alone the Ritz-Carlton or W or similar competitive offerings.The location is great and every associate we came into contact was professional and pleasant. The buffet-style food we had was just fine and priced right. Whoever is managing and operating Le Pavillion is doing a great job. Their owners need to step in a bit more with respect to the physical product, especially the room and bed.

<Author>nyc10029
<Content>Pretty good overall My wife and I stayed at Le Pavillon for five nights around Christmas. The hotel itself was very good (location not as much, more below). The entire staff was extremely helpful and friendly. The architectural design was superior, very ornate in both the lobby and the room itself. Because lots of restaurants were closed Christmas Eve and Christmas, we ordered a lot of room service, which was really good, and not too expensive. Free use of a computer with internet access on the 2nd floor was very convenient. We also booked a good tour of the city, including areas devastated by Katrina, through a recommendation by the hotel concierge, with Dixieland Tours. Only the sub-par view and the somewhat uncomfortable beds were drawbacks at the hotel.The biggest problem with the experience was the location. In a completely safe city that hadn't experienced a recent disaster, the 1500 or so feet between the hotel and one edge of the French Quarter would be insignificant, but as it stands you can't get between the two without passing lots of abandoned/boarded up office buildings. As the person checking us in said, it's a big city, and if you don't feel safe at night, call a cab. Which we did. That said, it was a convenient walk down Poydras to the river, and the St. Charles Streetcar stops nearby, but you can also get these advantages from French Quarter hotels. You definitely don't have to worry about loud music at two in the morning at Le Pavillon, though!

<Author>dfwtraveler
<Content>Anniversary trip My husband and I went to New Orleans for our anniversary Dec 26-28th. We booked our trip through Travelocity and got an outstanding rate at LePavillion. Easy cab ride to the beautiful hotel. Service was outstanding from the doorman to the concierge to housekeeping. We even noticed the front desk giving out umbrellas and rain panchos on a rainy morning. The hotel must be the most gorgeous hotel in all of New Orleans. We were upgraded to a deluxe King room on the 8th (next to the top) floor. Great room and bathroom, but the bathroom was on the small side. Location wise, it was a little farther from the French Quarter than I would have preferred. We walked to the Quarter without a problem, but there was nothing really nearby unless you were in town for business. We did not dine at the hotel, but did have drinks in the bar which was very nice. We ate at NOLA which is absolutely not to be missed, had beignets and coffee at Cafe Dumonde (long line), burger at Camilla Grill (another long line...but well worth it and the streetcar now goes all the way again) and dinner at GW Fins (very good). We listened to jazz at the Howlin Wolf. Would have enjoyed it more if we hadn't spent hours walking during the day, only to have to stand (large place with very limited tables/chairs). The next night we went to bar at the Ritz and really enjoyed the quieter, laid back atmosphere and being able to sit on a sofa, listen to some excellent jazz and have a nice glass of champagne.

<Author>taistrike
<Content>You could better I did extensive reviews on TA before booking this hotel, and I was extremely disappointed with the quality of the hotel. We booked from Expedia for $99/night (paid $10 for an upgraded room). Check in was fine, the front desk was cordial but not exceptionally nice. The front lobby is very beautiful and was decorated for very nicely for Christmas time. During our three day stay we encountered the following problems:1.) Room wasvsmall and not very attractively decorated. It was decorated in a faux 1800s style, but it looked like it was done with a $100 budget. From the gaudy table cloth that hung all over the floor, to the large and noticeably plastic plant on the armoire the room was just generally ugly. In addition it was extremely small, like NYC small. I have stayed in hundreds of hotel rooms in my life and this is one of the smallest. My girlfriend and I stumbled all over each other during the stay in the small room. It would help if instead of a table and 2 chairs they just left room to walk around, or put something more suitable, like a desk. I couldn't find a working outlet in the room without unplugging the lamps, and the heat was difficult to operate (some of that 17th century charm?), the toilet screeched for 30 seconds each time it was flushed, and finally a portion of the window in our room was cracked and covered with duct tape. Not what I expect from a 4-star hotel.2.) The staff does speak english as many have noted in previous posts, however they are not the friendliest or most outgoing people I have witnessed. We consulted the concierge as we left on Xmas Eve about what dinner options we might have without a reservation. Her exact response was good luck and pointed us at a couple of restaurants that might have available tables. We didn't expect a miracle (and realize that we were asking for one) but she just seemed to put forth no effort at all to help us. We ended up having a wonderful dinner at Gallatoire's which we ended up at due to our own research. The people who work the bar and breakfast were not much better, certainly all of them could have been nicer (and at times I considered borderline rude). I won't go on much as no one did anything particularly rude, but I wanted to counter the previous posts that said the staff were so exceptionally nice. In their defense, all of the people who worked the front door were really nice and helpful.3.) Breakfast, I will just say avoid it, at $18 there are tons of better options.In all the hotel was average at best, the rooms small and not decorated well, and the staff could do better. I would rank this 2-3 stars, book at your own risk.

<Author>HolaGatitos
<Content>It really is the "belle of New Orleans" I travel to New Orleans a lot and had not previously stayed at Le Pavillon---boy do I regret that. This really is a special place. The decor is wonderfully over-the-top Gilded Age everything. The public spaces are gorgeous. My room had all these amazing special touches....stenciling on the ceiling, wonderful molding, a porcelain shower head, a bathroom mirror that doesn't fog above the sink (how do they do that?), 60 some odd channels on the television, etc., etc.The hotel is elegant in every way. The bar and restaurant are beautiful and the late night PBJs are a great treat! And the staff....the only thing I can compare them to is what you find at the Ritz...elegant without being fussy, no one acts snotty, everything seems pleasant. This was a truly pleasurable stay and this doesn't even consider the price which I thought a mistake when I booked this hotel online. What a bargain! I know I'll be back.

<Author>braumeister
<Content>Unbeatable New Orleans experience Beautiful downtown hotel with great heritage (it turned 100 years old in 2007). A little on the ornate side, but extremely comfortable. The thing that struck me was that I don't think I've ever seen a hotel where every single person who worked there was so totally friendly and welcoming. The staff attitude is just simply fantastic, and it really added an extra dimension to my stay.Marvelous little extra amenities, like the peanut butter sandwiches at night, your choice of New Orleans newspaper in the morning or Wall St. Journal or NY Times. The hot tub in the fitness center is marvelous, with one of the best views of the city. Great restaurant in the hotel as well.Unfortunately, I had one bad experience when I left. I had reserved a space on the airport shuttle, and paid the concierge the $13 fee. He gave me a ticket and receipt. I handed the receipt to the shuttle van driver when he picked me up, and he said nothing until we got to the airport. Then he said I had to pay $11. I explained that I had paid the concierge $13, and the driver said I was supposed to pay him only $2, with the other $11 going to the van driver. I got a bit hostile, and the driver backed off, but it was very unpleasant. I still don't know who was right (the hotel concierge or the van driver), but I would advise double checking on this matter if you have to use the airport shuttle when leaving.

<Author>debracake
<Content>Great place! I booked on Hotwire and overpaid -- another guest used Priceline and got the room for $80. Bummer. However, the hotel is beautiful and comfortable and the service is excellent. <Content>Loved Le Pavillon! My friend found Le Pavillon during his travels to New Orleans for work. He raved about the service, quality of rooms, delicious breakfast buffet, and its location (downtown). He was right about everything! The service was wonderful. Though we should have been more specific about the type of place we were looking for, the restaurant we went to was not good at all. We were disappointed. Overall, if you are looking for a hotel, not in the French Quarter, this is it. Also, Le Pavillon is listed as one of America's historic hotels. Enjoy!

<Author>TravelBeard
<Content>Ornate public areas, disappointing rooms, friendly service Le Pavillon is an ornate, often grand hotel with gracious staff and disappointing rooms. The lobby, restaurant, bar and hallways are among the most impressive in New Orleans, with huge crystal chandeliers, high ceilings, elaborate statuary, and quarries of marble, as well as noteworthy paintings, and rich fabrics. Employees are delightful and welcoming. While name usage wasn鈥檛 great, every employee with whom I interacted was enthusiastic, friendly, and helpful. As well, it is clear that the staff takes great pride in their workplace.Hotel d茅cor will either delight or disappoint. While the over the top decoration works in the public areas, in the guestrooms, these flourishes may be too much. Tasseled valences over the shower curtain, for example, can be offputting to the point of being irritating.That said, the guestrooms are disappointing, in size and d茅cor. Unlike modern guestrooms鈥攖he building is over 100 years old鈥攖here is no entry alcove once you鈥檝e come into the room. So the room seems like a bit of a box, and a smallish one at that. The d茅cor鈥攇rand in large spaces鈥攕eems dated and stilted in a guestroom. The armoire eats up much of the room too鈥攁 flat screen TV would increase the perception of space a great deal. Bathroom, though nicely finished in marble, is small by today鈥檚 standards, and looks as if decorated by a drag queen. There was some wear issues鈥攁 badly maintained bathtub, for example鈥攂ut overall, housekeeping and engineering staff work to the place looking good. Air conditioning works well.On the rooftop, there is a small though nicely furnished fitness center, as well as a great swimming pool, whirlpool, and sundeck. Great place to spend a sunny day鈥攂ut tanners, note: There are only eight chaise lounges around the rather small pool.Overall, service is good, though one day, housekeeping overlooked cleaning our room, and for a luxury hotel, you might expect better name usage. Room service was prompt, but our name wasn鈥檛 used by the order taker or server, and the tray wasn鈥檛 picked up for hours. Breakfast was tasty, and room service for three ran about $63, with all of us feeling full.Hotel鈥檚 location is about 6 blocks from the beginning of Bourbon Street, in the area of downtown New Orleans convenient to some office buildings, about halfway between the Mississippi River and the Superdome. While nearby to many attractions, the blocks surrounding the hotel can be a bit desolate on nights and weekends, and based upon local recommendations, caution is advised walking back from the French Quarter after dark.Le Pavillon has many nice added value features. Fitness center usage, wireless internet, and nightly peanut butter sandwiches in the lobby are all complimentary to guests.This is a member of The Leading Hotels of the World, and by comparison, travelers used to the standards of other LHW hotels may find these rooms disappointing. In my opinion, the rooms are in need of renovation and updating, for certain.At full price, this hotel may disappoint given the rooms. I reserved the hotel for $53 a night on Priceline, so all of these amenities were a great value at this price鈥攖hough the rather noteworthy low Priceline rate was more likely an indication of the New Orleans hotel market and the slow Labor Day weekend than the state of the room product.Finally, New Orleans looks great, at least in the areas tourists are most likely to visit. The only evidence of Katrina damage in the downtown and French Quarter areas are a few boarded up hotels (neither the Hyatt nor the Fairmont have reopened) and a lack of tourism at times, included a once thriving riverfront mall鈥擱iverwalk--that is now 50% vacant and ill-visited. In some ways, the city is more appealing than ever for travelers鈥攁nd hotel values abound. If you have any doubt about a visit to New Orleans, look beyond them and by all means, make the trip. Not only will you have a wonderful time here, but nothing would hasten the recovery of this unique city than a return to previous tourism levels. . .

<Author>StevenandBrenda
<Content>Still the Best!!! We have just returned from our vacation in New Orleans and Houston. One night was spent at this beautiful hotel. The staff is very hospitable and professional. The rooms and baths are on the small side, but very nice with the traditional amenities. There is also a safe in the closet.  The public rooms are very ornate and include a row of huge crystal chandeliers from the front entry and lobby through the dining room. The pool and hot tub are on the roof. The view from the roof is fantastic at night. There are also cabanas, tables and chairs. This is the only area of the hotel that allows smoking. I believe smoking is no longer permitted inside any hotel or restaurant in Louisiana.  A breakfast buffet is served in the dining room. Pat is still there cooking omelets and singing!!! It was excellent, but expensive at $16.99 per person. Complimentary peanut butter and jelly sandwiches with hot chocolate are served in the lobby every night at 10:00 pm.  There is really nothing in the immediate vicinity to do. The French Quarter is about 3 blocks away. Four of us took a cab to the French Quarter at the corner of Bourbon and Canal street for less than $8.00. Go several blocks down Poydras toward the river and there are hotels and restaurants. The Hilton and The Riverwalk Mall are at the end of Poydras with Harrahs Casino across the Street.  Parking at the hotel is easy and safe. The lot is beside the hotel and is $28.00 per day for self or valet parking.  This was our second visit to Le Pavillon, but not our last. The service was great from the door man dressed in his great white hunter outfit to Pat singing in the dining room as she prepared our eggs.  We booked our 2 rooms through Hotwire for $72.00 per room. This was less than what we paid in 1994.

<Author>DeeJon
<Content>Nice decor, staff and food needs some work I was in New Orleans over night and decided to stay at Le Pavillon. I read otehr reviews and it sounded prefect for my one night stay. I got to the hotel about midngiht so I missed the peanut butter and jelly, so I order room service instead. At first I ordered the slad that was on the menu. They told me it would be about 30 mins. While I thought this was a long wait, I said ok. After about 20 mins. they called to say they didn't have salad. Strange but ok, I ordered the gumbo instead. Now I'm from Louisiana (living in California now) so I may set a higher standard for gumbo than most, but there is no way they could call what they gave me gumbo, especially seafood gumbo. First there was no seafood at all. Secondly, there was no rice and this stuff was so thick, I could have plastered the walls. Then to top it off, it was cold! At this point, I'm so tried, I just go to sleep. i was meeting a friend for breakfast using the two breakfast meals that were suppose to cal with the room (I booked it through the hotel web site. It was one of their sepcial deals). But when I looked in the envelope, there was only one ticket. I called the front deck and asked about the other ticket only to be told that becasue I was the only person registered, that I could only get one ticket. Whne I explained that the offered said I would get 2, the responses was, will you need to let us know this in advance. Very begouningly she gave me the other breakfast ticket. The foodd was standard fare, but the setting was very nice.Then I decide to work off some of that breakfast food in their gym. The gym very hard to find. You go to the top floor then walk down the hall hoping to see a sign to point you in the right direction. Then you go through a door up some stairs and through another door. The gym is small, but had the basic equipment. One big problem however, they had a nice refrigerator, but no water in it. Nor was there a water fountain. In fact, I ended up going back to my room to get some water.So now it's time to check out. I checked my bill and noticed they charged me for parking, which was suppose to be included in the rate I paid (again, part of the special). After she checked this out with her boss and everyone else behind the desk, they finally determined I was right and didn't have to pay again. I nicest treatment I got was from the bell captain. He was extremely nice and very helpful. I've heard that service in New Orleans has gone down since the hurrcaine. If this is an example, I would agree. I had not been here since Katrina, but I travel here quite a bit before and this is the worst service (and food) I have ever had. I would give them another chance to turn times around becasue I want to support the area in any way I can, but I think the hotel needs to work with training the staff a bit more. And really work on improving the food. Beautiful hootel, bad service.

<Author>Irishgirl1969
<Content>Order, Elegance, Pleasure, Peace, and Opulence The words from my review title are from Arthur Rimbaud. He was a French Romantic Poet. He knew some things about Beauty and Romance. If you are interested in these things then you too will Love Le Pavillon.Le Pavillon is Gorgeous. It is full of Antiques, Antique Art, Chandeliers, Marble and Beautiful Rugs. I have a lifelong interest in Antiques, and I decided to stay in The Victorian Suite, because the pictues of it were so Lovely. It was Fabulous. The Antiques were Beautiful, and the two handcarved Rosewood beds are fit for a King and a Queen. The Food is Yummy. The Lounge is Lovely and furnishes Entertainment. The rooftop Pool is truly---off the hook----. There are a couple of Private cabanas available for those who get lucky. I was able to get one. The Pool is very, very clean, as is the entire Pool and sundeck area.I also stayed in The Mallard Suite. It has an Antique Canopy Bed and a Jacuzzi. It is smallish, but very well-appointed. The Jacuzzi was clean and in perfect working order. The Marble in the bathrooms at Le Pavillon is Gorgeous. The Wallpaper, Bedding, Drapes, and Rugs are all very nice looking. I appreciate Beauty, and I also like Beautiful Behavior. The staff at Le Pavillon is Incredibly Nice, and they know what they are doing. The place runs like a well-oiled machine. I always got my Food done correctly and served at the right temperature. The cleanliness was Very Good, and this is coming from a Nurse folks, so it isn't easy to pass my inspection.You cannot expect to stay in a 100 year old place that it full of Antiques and not find some dust here or there. I will take a spot of dust in return for what Massive Luxury Le Pavillon offers. This is a five star Hotel and it is a One Of A Kind On This Earth. I give them my official A in all categories. There is no better thing in America than getting what you pay for, and Le Pavillon is not cheap. You pay a high price for Massive Beauty and Privacy. Sign me up for next year too, and every year after that. I'm in Love.

<Author>JonesPro
<Content>Le Pavillon THE PLACE TO STAY in NOLA My wife and I just returned from a one night stay at the Le Pavillon in New Orleans (4-18-07) for a quick get away. ( what!?!? Get away to New Orleans!) Absolutely! New Orleans is really begining to come around, especially down town and the french quarter. (EAST NEW ORLEANS STILL LOOKS LIKE BAGHDAD) We have NEVER had service like we had at Le Pavillion. The PBJ bar between 10:00 and 11:00 is a hit! The restaurant looked great although we opted for lunch at Court of Two Sisters for lunch and Dickie Brennans Steak House for Dinner. If you are concerned about the location being in down town... DON'T. My wife was wheel chair bound and we walked at night from the hotel to the french quarter on a wednesday night no problem (however, the hotel staff are only too ready to hail a cab for you, and Cabs are everywhere in the french quarter so you can cab back to the hotel in approx 3 mins). The city has installed super bright street lights and you really dont feel like your security is breached. Police are EVERYWHERE IN THE FRENCH QUARTER so you feel safe there as well, I mean, you see like 2-3 officers on every block and cop cars everywhere.  It seems like NOLA is doing a fine job to make the quarter more safe and more fun than before Katrina.  The roof top pool area is very nice - we had drinks (hurricanes) delivered to us pool side - PERFECT. There are also 2 cabanas for you and your honey to get out of the sun and away from the people)  Our room (king deluxe) was LARGE and ULTRA CLEAN! Also the mini bar was well stocked with snacks and drinks. The shower is AWESOME! Overall the hotel is Authentic European French... The ENTIRE STAFF goes way beyond their payscale to make your stay pleasant.  I would reccomend the Le Pavillon to EVERYONE! Including business travelers - Free FAST Internet and close to down town offices as well. Enjoy the Le Pavillon!

<Author>cliquot
<Content>Le Pavillion's impressive service A smaller hotel doing a fine job, Le Pavilion was a great all-around experience. The hotel is walking distance (4 blocks) from the quarter, in a safe, well-lit area of the central business district. New Orleans Arena is also walking distance. We upgraded to a junior suite for a very reasonable price ($40 per night) from the regular room that we booked. The suite wasn't huge, but was well appointed and comfortable. Toiletries were above average, and the rainfall shower-jacuzzi tub were great after a long day of walking.Didn't try the restaurant (too many great restaurants to try), but the piano bar was nice. The reason to return is the service. A frequent traveler to upscale hotels, I was still impressed by the civility, thoughtfulness, and genuine warmth from the staff.This is not a chain experience, and I mean that in the best sense of the phrase!

<Author>MdChowhound
<Content>Warm hospitality, great location and room I had the opportunity to stay in New Orleans for a conference in March '07, and my stay at Le Pavillon was fantastic. This hotel is located in the Central Business District, with a short walk to the SuperDome, French Quarter and RiverWalk.The property is meticulously maintained, from the rooftop pool and veranda to the public spaces to the rooms themselves. The service I received was very attentive, courteous, yet warm and personal as well. Everyone we met with greeted us with a smile and helped with everything from personal accommodations for our room to restaurant reservations.One unique service this hotel provides is the nightly snack time of peanut butter and jelly sandwiches, hot chocolate, fruit and fresh bread. This long standing tradition is just one example of the southern hospitality we received on our trip.I would like to visit New Orleans again in the near future to see more of the city (I was only able to see the French Quarter and Garden District this time around) and I will have no qualms about staying at Le Pavillon again.

<Author>KR
<Content>Old Glory, off the beaten path but walking distance to the FQ (daytime only) I don't have much time to write a review, except to say the staff is exceptional in most cases. This is an old hotel, on the Natl Registry of Historic Places (or Hotels, something like that). So don't expect six elevators, but DO expect an awesome buffet served up by a woman you wish you'd had as a nanny, and quirks such as peanut butter cookie treats (and sandwiches in the lobby nightly). I stayed there one night and loved the place and its history...my room had an electric fireplace and a wet bar, but with creaky floors and the noisy elevator shaft nearby, I doubt it'd be my choice for an extended business stay.

<Author>fifigirl
<Content>We will be back! Le Pavillon is a beautiful and elegant hotel. The room we had was not fancy, but clean and comfortable, but the rest of the hotel is gorgeous. The bed was a pillowtop and we slept well, plus it was very quiet in the hotel. We enjoyed the rooftop pool and poolside service very much. We only ate once in the restaurant and it was good, not excellent, but good. There are many good restaurants close by. Mother's is just down the street and if you like oysters you have got to try theirs. The staff was very helpful and efficient. There are supposedly ghosts in the hotel but I was a little disappointed we didnt see one. When we come back to NO, we will definitely be staying at Le Pavillon.

<Author>lhusseini
<Content>Not at ALL what I expected My husband and I picked Le Pavillion b/c a couple of friends mentioned it was a nice hotel and it was centrally located for us (quick ride from airport, 10 minute walk to French Quarter from hotel, etc.). The front desk staff was very pleasant, they even upgraded our room when we checked in. Although the exterior of the hotel looks nice, and the lobby is definitely impressive, the rooms need updating DESPARATELY. First off, the bed was extremely lumpy and old. The HVAC in our room was poor; the room was stuffy, so we turned on the AC, but it made a rattling noise the entire time we had it on (in addition to the bed, it was very difficult to sleep). When we left the room, housekeeping would turn up the heat (the weekend we were down there was unusually cold for NO) and the room would be stuffy again. The bedding was dated (blankets were cheap and our pillows were flat...literally, you could fold them in half and they weren't supportive at all) and carpeting was dingy. The bathrooms are very small and the shower fixtures are old and covered in soap scum. Overall, I was not impressed by the hotel. The service was fine, the front desk staff was the most pleasant; the conceirge could take a lesson or two from them in the personality department.

<Author>IADDutch
<Content>Very disappointed This is NOT a 4 1/2 star hotel, I would give it 3 stars at best!We went for a long weekend to NOLA, and based on the reviews I expected to spend 4 nights at a grand, classic hotel with all the services that one would expect at a place like this. Well, let me tell you what I found.There is no spa. No coffee maker in the room. The 'updated' room I booked was run down and old. When I asked for another room, they suggested a room with two queens instead of a king - how romantic. The exercise room was in disrepair. The pool was closed for maintenance. The elevators were less than clean. On saturday night, the bar and restaurant were closed for a private party, only room service available. Three out of four nights, the turndown service either didn't happen, or wasn't done right. One evening we found cleaning supplies on the floor in the middle of the room. What could have been a great weekend ended up as a great disappointment.Oh, and by the way, with the current crime problem in NOLA, it is too far from the french quarter to walk. <Author>TravellingLawyerNYC
<Content>Outstanding Staff and a Best Buy A completely-independent property like this can only survive on strong word of mouth, and after staying four nights here, I can see why this one consistently earns such allocates from TripAdvisor reviewers. I had high expectations after reading the TA reviews, and the hotel did not disappoint. La Pavillon offers old-timey essence-of-hospitality service and an irreplaceable Grande Dame decor, with suprisingly-modern amenities, like free Wi-Fi (and wired) Internet and dual-line, direct-inward-dial room phones. Hands-down a Best Buy. The superb concierges have outstanding knowlege, recommendations, and character: when my girlfriend left thousands of dollars of jewelry on the nightstand while we rushed to a swamp tour, the Chief Concierge offered personally to retrieve it and lock it in the hotel safe, genuinely-happy to have saved us hours of worry. Our four days zipped by as we explored tours and trips, the best of which were the ones recommended by the Concierges: our guide on the Cajun Honey Island swamp tour was outstanding, as was the small boat he used; our walking-tour guide in the Garden District and cemetary was the best I have ever experienced, the jazz club the concierge recommended on Frenchman's Street was first-rate. These were truly the most knowledgeable and thoughtful concierges I have had the pleasure of dealing with at any hotel anywhere, ever. They weren't trip-sellers; they were educated, articulate people who knew and loved their city and knew exactly how to help you experience it.Only a hotel that has been there for one hundred years could so consistently do everything right, including doing all sorts of little things to let you know how much they appreciate your business. When a bulb burned out in the bathroom, maintenance was there literally in five minutes. Room service was quick and delicious, a cut above what you'd find at a chain hotel. Every staff member we encountered was warm, willing, and acted like it was his or her privilege to help us, offering zillions of little kindnesses during our trip. Maid service was quick and flawless, and the extensive, quality selection of toiletries and such harkened back to when hotels really wanted you to have and use this stuff, and bring it home to spread their name. The PBJ tradition is inspired, and is a nice opportunity to share raves about this gem with other guests. Cabs are readily-available, but the location makes walking to the Riverwalk, the Aquarium, the Quarter and the CBD all very easy. I should say that the hotel does not offer stuffy, oh-so-refined-but-just-a-little-condescending service like some high-end chains. Rather, it offers genuinely-competent, genuinely-caring, genuinely-friendly service that is there the moment you seek it and sometimes even before you think to ask for it. There is no question that we will be back.  
<Date>Jan 3, 2007

<Author>pittgirl99
<Content>Wonderful stay! My husband and I took a trip to New Orleans to celebrate our first anniversary -- and we were not disappointed. <Content>Big Dirty in the Big Easy I stayed at the Hotel Le Pavillon in August with my family of four. We booked a luxury two bedroom suite to allow the children to sleep in a separate bedroom. Upon arrival there was no bellman or valet to be found. It took several minutes to check in as they had misplaced our reservation. We were upgraded to the antique suite. Upon arrival in the suite I was distressed tohave an empty bottle of Jack Daniels fall on my head whilst retrieving the only extra pillow in the room from the closet shelf. (A total of four small pillows had been provided for two queen beds). I asked that housekeeping send extra pillows and retrieve the empty bottle of liquor and the housekeeper arrived disgruntled and scowling, clearly upset to be doing her job.I then went into one of two bathrooms to wash my hands and was dismayed to see a thick, thick layer of dirt on the wall and floor. I took a wash cloth and ran it along the floor under the sink and floorboard and it was covered in filth and a great deal of someone else's hair. I quickly went to the other bathroom and discovered an equally disturbing level of filth. At this point I called and voiced my concerns to the manager who once again sent housekeeping to take care of the problem. At this point someone did come and scrub but they did not bother to replacae any of the washcloths I had used with new ones.In addition the the dirt it turns out that one is charged when anything in the mini bar is touched. I know this is a practice in several places however we have never had so much trouble getting the charges reversed. Finally, while I do not expect every hotel to carry uber expensive toiletries, I do expect that a 400 dollar per night suite would provide shampoo and conditioner and not a watery conditioning shampoo. I was completely disappointed by my experience at this hotel. It is Not because this is an older hotel; one of my favorite hotels in the world is the famed Pink Hotel in Honolulu and several other older hotels are dear to my heart. However, being older should not preclude being clean.

<Author>RTGeorgia
<Content>Great Experience My son and I stayed at Le Pavillion for two nights over the Labor Day weekend.  We had a very smooth check-in and arrived in our room to find a fruit and bottled water basket with balloons and a personal note from the hotel. The room was gorgeous and clean with none of the musty smells mentioned in some reviews. The rooftop pool was beautiful and the view was great. The staff was helpful and friendly. It is very rare that a hotel is actually nicer than you expect, but this was one of those rare occasions. I have recommended this hotel to everyone I have talked to since returning.

<Author>rohese
<Content>A Disaster I came to New Orleans for a 2 month stay as a contractor working for a government agency, and long-term housing at LePavillon was provided. At first, the chandeliers and the lobby promised a luxury experience, but it only took a few hours to dispel those expectations! As other reviews have already made clear, the bedrooms and bathrooms are dirty, musty - the whole hotels smells like mold - the bedding is old and worn-out, and the temperature controls don't work. The hotel staff has obviously been well-versed as to what constitutes southern hospitality, but in spite of this overweening solicitousness (within five minutes, staff is calling you by your first name), they cannot be relied on to execute requests for simple wake-up calls or other basic services. Rooms and restaurant are overpriced, the food is mediocre, and the hotel is generally half-empty. Requests for better mattresses are ignored by the managerial staff; the hotel bills you for incidentals without your knowledge or without submitting the list of incidentals they are billing you for to you in advance (my daughter and her son were substantially overbilled for mini-bar charges they did not incur). In my own mini-bar, I discovered an opened, half-drunken bottle of white wine - which, while I reported it, has not been removed or replaced in over 3 weeks! Dirty moldy interiors, worn-out bedding, unresponsive management, and sloppy billing - check in at your own risk!

<Author>nolaguest
<Content>Nice but not worth the $$ We were guests this past weekend, in a Junior Suite at $229.00 per night. Check-in was very slow and cumbersome. The Front Desk clerk stated they were not expecting anyone in their Junior Suites over the weekend so he would have to send housekeeping to a suite and check on the condition (I was very surprised by this considering we had a reservation for a Junior Suite). It took half an hour to obtain entrance to the room.The room was classic Victorian in decor. However, there were flaws. The couch was worn, the carpet was split, and the bed was extremely soft. All-in-all the room was musty. There was an atmosphere of old world charm but the condition of the room did not meet the rate.Dinner in the hotel restaurant was memorable because it felt like a walk-in freezer! All guests were complaining about the temperature. The food was OK ... not great, not bad ... but did not rise to the $97.00 bill for Dinner (two entrees, two soft drinks, two bowls of soup).Drinks served in the hotel lounge were well mixed and comparable to the pricing.The much-advertised peanut butter and jelly sandwich with hot chocolate and milk offering at 10:00PM was interesting. We walked into the lobby at 10:10PM to find 80% of the sandwiches gone, only skim milk served in pint cartons available, and barely enough hot chocolate in the container to pour one drink. It's a great idea and nice touch but at least don't run out of everything in ten minutes (on a night when the hotel's staff told me they were running about 40% occupancy).The Breakfast buffet was tasty and well prepared. And at $18.00 per person it should have been.All-in-all I'm glad we stayed, it was a unique experience, but I doubt we'll be back due to the apparent decline of the property. I highly suggest the owners invest in new carpeting and bedding in the rooms.

<Author>J_Thornhill
<Content>In Terms of Luxury, Le Pavillon Falls Short of the Mark The uniformly glowing reviews of this property make me even more regretful that my own visit was not nearly as enjoyable. I visited in March of 2005, on my first visit to New Orleans. To be fair, it should be stated that I checked in at the Pavillon after more than a week at the Maison Orleans, arguably one of the finest hotels in the south, owned and operated by the adjacent Ritz-Carlton. Nonetheless, I had been seduced by the gorgeous website and with a few more days in the city, I was hopeful that the Pavillon would offer a change of scenery. It certainly did.The hotel鈥檚 exterior is nothing less than breathtaking, especially at night, standing in sharp contrast to the relatively modern buildings of the business district. Unfortunately, the exterior is where my happy memories of this hotel end. The lobby might be described as grand if one has little experience with grandeur. Yes, there was plenty of marble and several chandeliers, yet these things alone do not define luxury. Close inspection of nearly any area reveals the use of inexpensive materials and a lack of attention to detail 鈥?tell-tale signs of a renovation budget spread painfully thin. It may have been thought charming and no doubt economical to retain the ancient and disarming check-in 鈥渃age鈥? but the installation of a more modern and welcoming reception area would have proven a much wiser investment. The check-in process itself was a decidedly dull affair, not unlike a visit to the DMV, with the agent exhibiting only the barest modicum of hospitality. Carrying my own bags to my room, the elevator opened onto a poorly-lit and dingy hallway which had apparently been overlooked during the recent 鈥渕ulti-million dollar renovations鈥?touted in the brochures. Gaudy murals could not hide the obvious neglect. Not surprisingly, the room itself perfectly met each of my already low expectations. Red and green jewel tones dominated the d茅cor revealing an even more futile attempt at 鈥渙ld-world鈥?opulence. The Pavillon has obviously yet to learn the lesson that true luxury cannot be mass-produced. Try to imagine a 鈥淭reasures from Old New Orleans鈥?hour on the Home Shopping Network, and you will begin to understand my disappointment. The staff was as attentive and professional as one might expect them to be without proper training. Most seemed to go about their duties with an air of awkward confusion; inoffensive, but not terribly helpful. I recall some bewilderment regarding my ability to take breakfast in the main dining room. Some misguided young couple had apparently decided to celebrate the happiest day of their lives in that room, and paying guests were being re-routed to the bar area for breakfast in preparation for the event. I and several other guests naturally refused, and remained in limbo for about fifteen minutes before finally being allowed inside. The staff in the dining room were friendly, though subject to a rather unorthodox ranking system which provided some servers with 鈥渁ssistants鈥? a situation I have yet to encounter again. I would note however, that the breakfast itself was quite good.My only consolation for the 鈥淧avillon Affair鈥?(as I now refer to it) is that my overall experience in the beautiful Crescent City was enjoyable due to the warm, welcoming and wonderful people who live there. In terms of accommodations, the city is filled with any number of delightful hotels and BB鈥檚. To make your visit to New Orleans the delight it ought to be, I would recommend staying somewhere other than Le Pavillon.

<Author>sjblackman
<Content>Neat experience! First trip to NOLA; did a lot of research before booking. Thought pictures looked beautiful - was not disappointed. It was in walking distance to many things; a $5 cab ride will get you to the French Quarter.The staff was extremely friendly and interested in our stay. I was a little concerned when I walked in with my two small children (2 and 3 yrs old) because the place is like a muesem! But no one seemed to care that I had two munchkins in tow - in fact, many people stopped to talk to both of them.Housekeeping staff was very friendly! Always asked me how things were when I saw them. Hotel room was the typical setup, but with plenty of crown molding and other nice touches that made it seem more like a bed and breakfast.The breakfast buffet, although pricey, was nice. I was full until late afternoon. At least go look at the dining room - it is lovely.Pool was beautiful. It might be considered a little small, but it was only myself and one other family, so it was plenty of space.My kids LOVED the peanut butter reception. Was a nice, quaint touch in such an R rated city. Everyone mingled around feel-good sandwiches and hot chocolate. Again, made it seem like a BB.Negatives - VERY expensive food in mini-bar. Don't even tough it b/c it's monitered by infared lasers. My husband found a spider the size of Mount Everest in the sink. Otherwise, very clean.
