<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not as impressed as others... This was my first trip back to New Orleans after evacuating the Saturday before Katrina. I chose to stay at Le Pavillon because of the rave reviews. Maybe I caught them on a bad weekend because I was not that impressed. The hotel lobby IS beautiful, the room was nice, but the decorative pillows on the beds were worn and torn. Our bathroom was not cleaned well after our first night (of four). We took our 3 month old son for his first swim in the rooftop pool (which is small but lovely) and there were no towels. I called the front desk and was told they would bring them right up; 45 minutes later we had to wrap our shivering infant in a hotel robe because there still were no towels. The hot chocolate was delicious (much better than the peanut butter and jelly sandwiches on slightly stale bread and bruised apples served with it), but hot chocolate does not a quality hotel make in my opinion. They also charged us for valet service we did not use (this was cleared right up). I expected much more for $150/night. I will try another hotel on our next visit as we try to get set to start our lives over in New Orleans.  
<Date>May 14, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Le Pavillon: Grand Lobby/ Great Service We booked our room at Le Pavillon on Expedia not sure how we would find the hotel or the City of New Orleans 6 months after Katrina. We're happy to report that the hotel suffered no ill effects from the storm and the city is rallying. The hotel is beautiful and offers the perfect balance of grandeur and treating everyone like an honored guest. My family, including 2 kids (11 and 13) arrived in New Orleans early Saturday, March 25, and went directly to a neighborhood cleanup effort. We arrived at the hotel looking a little hot and scruffy in sweats, jeans and caps. Despite our appearance, we were welcomed like royalty. The lobby, halls and rooms are beautiful and the service here -- and throughout the city -- was incredibly warm and welcoming. If we sensed anything, it was a lingering worry and weariness over Katrina, but the City is definitely coming back. Do not hesitate to come to New Orleans and you can't go wrong at Le Pavillon.  
<Date>Mar 30, 2006

<Author>torontotravellers5
<Content>Very Ornate Hotel, But a Few Caveats We enjoyed our 4-night stay immensely. As others have said, it is an exceptionally well-decorated hotel. In fact, we were informed by numerous locals that even they go there to enjoy the ambience.It was an excellent value (just over $100/night) because we were willing to suffer through the summer heat in New Orleans. (yeah, its pretty bad) For our price, we were completely satisfied with our stay- its now a memorable part of our trip. However, I don't think I would pay full price for the following reasons: Its not that close to the French Quarter (20 minute walk...at least), small rooms (and even smaller bathroom), expensive parking (yeah, its a big city, but when you see how insecure their lot is and when you realize that you're going to have to cab to the French Quarter fairly frequently, you'll get a little annoyed)Still, a remarkable hotel that truly spoils its clients and gives them a taste of New Orleans history....just consider the above caveats.

<Author>irvoc_78
<Content>Nice but inconsistent hotel Stayed at the Le Pavillon the weekend before Katrina hit New Orleans (Aug 26th-28th) - booked off of the hotel's website for a very good rate of $109/night. The hotel lobby was beautiful and immaculate, the previous reviewer was not kidding in saying it was the coldest room in New Orleans (and trust me, that's a good thing!). Perhaps I dealt with staff in all the off times, but I wasn't particularly impressed with the service anywhere in the hotel. It took almost 20 minutes for the valet to park my car upon check-in, it was 1 am and there practically a line of cars waiting. For $28/night you could do better, also note from what I saw the parking was outside. I'd at least expect the cars to be parked in a structure. However, the room was beautiful with high ceilings, a nice ceiling fan and crown molding. Bed was comfortable, but the bedding itself was not, a little stratchy from what I can remember. Also the previous reviewer said the bathroom was small...boy were they not kidding. I am not a big person by any means and I felt clausterphobic in there! And the shower/tub drain didn't work right, if I took any longer than a 10 minute shower the tub was almost half full of water! Also for a hotel of this caliber I was surprised to find shampoo/conditioner combo bottle. On the plus side, the gym while small is nicely stocked with fruit, water and sports beverages and the machines are adequate enough for a decent workout (albeit the equipment is a little old). The rooftop pool is a nice touch, with great views of the city. The pool could use some work though...some of the tiles have fallen off the pool. Unfortunately I wasn't there for the peanut butter and jelly sandwiches, must admit that is a nice touch. Check-out was a bit hectic to say the least...the valet brought out the wrong rental car and the front desk staff was abrupt and curt at best. Given the situation on Sunday morning (hurricane hit on Monday) I would let any establishment slide. Probably wouldn't stay at Le Pavillon again although I wish the hotel and the rest of New Orleans the best of luck and would like to say that it is a wonderful city and would love to visit again.  
<Date>Sep 8, 2005

<Author>wakegirl1967
<Content>Service, Smiles, and Snacks We just returned from a weekend getaway to New Orleans. We booked our package with Expedia and we were concerned that we might not be treated as well as someone who booked with the hotel directly. I called two weeks in advance to order flowers for my sweetie. Ms. Lou, the Concierge, said that we should order them the day before arrival to ensure that everything went smoothly. She took down my number and called me by 9 a.m. just as promised. When we arrived, after a thrilling cab ride from the airport (If you get an ex professional soccer player from Guatamala buckle up FAST), we were greeted by the valet and escorted into the hotel to the reception desk. We were upgraded from a room with a queen bed to a king bed! Our bell hop, Naheed, always greeted us and asked us how our stay was going. He was a wealth of information for things to do off the beaten path and for great local restaurants to eat at. The room was beautifully decorated and had adequate space for our needs. Yes the bathroom counter was small but I easily was able to put my belongings there without worry. Besides exactly how much time do you really spend in the bathroom? The safe was locked so we couldn't use it right away so we called down to the front desk and within a minute someone was at our door to fix it for us. We then went to have a cocktail before our balmy walk to dinner. Definitely request turndown service. Not only will you get a bedtime snack and a bottle of Abita Springs water (great for after an evening of a few too many cocktails)j but the maid will replace any used towels and replenish your shampoo, body lotion, and soap. Also make sure to have the late evening snack of PB  J's from 10 - 11. There were plenty of fixings to make your own sandwich plus fruit, superb hot chocolate, and ice cold milk. The Concierge, Ms. Lou was always helpful and can get you a reservation anywhere in town even on short notice! Also speak with any of the valets or bell hops they also have a good pulse on the city and can steer you in the right direction for a funky little place to eat or listen to wonderful music. My husband is a triatha-geek. So he found the workout facilities adequate for his needs. The pantry in the workout room is always stocked with sports drinks, bottled water and fresh fruit. Even if you don't use the facility you can go in for a snack in the m iddle of the afternoon to hold you over until dinner. The pool was small still refreshing after a hot day. YES, the elevators are slow but try to remember that the hotel was built in 1907. I'm sure part of what attracted to you to the property is the fact it is a historic property. If you want a faster elevator go to one of the newer chain hotels in the city. YES, it is a short walk to the Quarter but I would much rather take a walk to the Quarter or $5 cab ride so I could get a good nights sleep and not hear drunk people pounding up and down the halls all night long. Or to hear police sirens on Canal. It is a beautifully restored hotel whos charm is not only in the decor but the people who work there. I would definitely stay at this hotel again. p.s. The suite near room 728 has one of Napoleon Bonaparte's marble bathtubs. The people who were staying in there were kind enough to let us see the suite.

<Author>travelfromric
<Content>service charm style at Le Pavillion We just returned from two 2-day stays at Le Pavillion. What a lovely property! The lobby and downstairs is quite grand but elegant, and the rooftop pool is just stunning (fitness center is small, but nice, as well). There is obviously quite a bit of attention to detail here. The service was great--we gave the concierge staff a workout and they did a fine job for us, following up on a number of requests. The room (we had a deluxe room both times, on different floors, one w/ king, one w/ 2 queens) is quite nice. I particularly liked the painted ceiling (subtle, but charming). The bathrooms are small but very well-appointed, my only quibble being no place to hang the towel except a hook on the back of the door.During summer, this was excellent price for value as well. We found the location to be great for both the FQ and the warehouse district--you can get to both easily from the hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Comparable to the Ritz On our recent trip to New Orleans, we had decided to stay at the Le Pavillion Hotel. One of the first things that struck me was the professionalism and friendliness of the ENTIRE hotel staff. If you made eye contact they would smile, and greet you. They had a sense of pride about their hotel and were very quick to tell all kinds of information and stories about it. Whatever our needs were they were quickly met. The rooms were very well furnished, and the bathrooms with marble floors and sinks made you think you were in a palace. The rooms while very nice and comfortable, were a bit small, but so are many other comparable hotels. I was able to use the high speed internet with no problems at all. We didn't like some of the resturants we went to in town, so one night we had ordered room service. The food was better than some of the resturants on Bourbon street, and the price was cheaper, so we had room service for the rest of our time there. I very stongly recommend ordering breakfast. This was our second trip to New Orleans, our first stay was at the Ritz. I can honestly say that our experiance at the Le Pavillion was comparable to that of the Ritz. The Le Pavillion is way more economical than the Ritz, making it more appealing and a better bargin than the Ritz.

<Author>GinaDRacine
<Content>Great Hotel This hotel is a wonderful place to stay in the cess pool of downtown New Orleans. It's an older hotel that has spent untold dollars to ensure luxury at an affordable price. The rooms are somewhat small, but not uncomfortable. The decor is beautiful and the shower was the best I've ever experienced. The shower head dumps loads of water that feels similar to standing under a waterfall. (not stinging; pouring). The bath area is all marble and the swinging glass shower door is very unusual. The concierge is extremely helpful and gives tourist advice, brochures, and good directions. The breakfast buffet is high priced, but well worth it. (about $17). The restaurant (The Crystal Room) is beautiful, but expensive. I would highly recommend at least one meal during your stay. They serve excellent food. The rooftop pool and hot tub are nice, but small. The workout area is very nice. They even have a small fridge full of water and sports drinks, and a basket of fresh fruit (all free) for hotel guests who use the facility. The tradition of serving free peanut butter and jelly sandwiches, hot chocolate, fruit, and milk in the lobby every night is great! We really enjoyed our stay. Parking costs $28 per night (typical in New Orleans), and the valet parking service is ccontracted out by the hotel. The first night we were there, the valet parked our rental car by a wall and put a huge scratch on it. I would recommend parking your car yourself.

<Author>Bimini Twist
<Content>Our Fave, For Lots of Reasons My husband, son, and I often stay in New Orleans when visiting family nearby. Over the years, we've lodged in many hotels in the Big Easy...and Le Pavillon, a small, European-style luxury hotel in the Central Business District, continues to be our favorite. The location on Poydras is ultra-convenient, close to the French Quarter, Garden District, and Interstate 10. The European decor is elegant and luxurious (the dining room is billed as the most beautiful room in New Orleans, and that's not much of an overstatement...high praise in a city full of beautiful rooms). As with most close-in New Orleans hotels, standard rooms tend to be on the small side, but the beds are comfy, the linens soft, the marble baths clean and well-stocked, and the central air conditioning reliable (a must, at least six months of the year, in N.O.!). There's also a rooftop workout room, pool and Jacuzzi. We've found the employees to be unfailingly courteous and professional, and the concierge staff are some of the best in town. And while we rarely eat in any New Orleans hotel (not that they're bad, it's just that New Orleans has some of the best restaurants in America), we do recommend the breakfast buffet at Le Pav...it's quick and convenient for hotel guests, and Chef Pat's Bananas Foster waffles are unique and the ultimate brunch indulgence. Chef Pat is a one-of-a-kind lady as well. We recommend you check out Le Pav...and if you're on a budget, note that unlike some New Orleans luxury hotels, Le Pav often has Internet or seasonal specials.  
<Date>Jun 28, 2005

<Author>clkhls3x
<Content>Great service! Le Pavillon is a gorgeous hotel, and the staff is falling all over themselves to help you. We got a free upgrade and really enjoyed our stay. The pool area (on the roof) was lots of fun and a great place to hang out late at night (it's open until 1:00 am). The only drawback I found was the distance from the Quarter. <Author>caserbin
<Content>LePav Is Great We stayed at LePav in early June and overall enjoyed our time there. One of the elevators was broken the entire time we were there so it made getting to and from our room a bit tedious, we often took the stairs as it was much faster than waiting. Our room was decorated beautifully but was smaller than I had expected. We had a deluxe queen. If you are used to room sizes at large, new hotels this will seem small. Everything in the room was clean and the evening turn down service was great. Even left us complimentary bottled water and cookies. The gym area is good with decent equipment. The pool area was less impressive. The photographs on the website are taken at night because in the day you would see how teeny tiny it is. It is a very small pool and there were only about ten lounge chairs. The staff at LePav was wonderful, very helpful and great about making recommendations. We frequently walked to the French Quarter and felt safe in the neighborhood. We are typically Marriott patrons but enjoyed the LePav as a nice diversion.

Le Pavillon was everything I expected, very elegant and full of art and beautiful furnishings, did not feel like a bull in a china shop at all. The pool is excellent, went up after a long day walking the FQ. The jacuzzi was an added treat. And don't forget the peanut butter and hot chocolate everynight at 10 pm. Staff were courteous and made our stay enjoyable. Would of loved to stay longer but wanted the Bourbon experience and stayed at the Royal Sonesta another 2 nights.

<Content>Always A Pleasure The staff was incredibly helpful. We got great restaurant tips --and reservations; the maids respected the Privacy Please signs; the breakfasts and lunches --prepared for a group-- were well above average.My only complaint is that the WiFi did not extend above the fifth floor (although we were assured that it worked in each and every room -- it worked for none of our group); and the ethernet was out of commission for almost our entire stay.Also, the elevators are incredibly slow; and there are occasions when one is aware of what is transpiring in the room next door.Still, the drawbacks are minor compared with the joy of staying in a beautifully restored, landmark hotel.This is our second stay at Le Pavillion; we have recommended that our group again select the hotel for its conference.

<Author>edknees
<Content>Very nice place I checked in quickly and efficiently and went to my room. I had asked for a non-smoking room but upon entering the room it smelled of cigarette smoke not unlike a French Quarter dive bar. I went back to the registration desk and said I had requested a non-smoking room. She replied that all the rooms wre non-smoking. Well, here in lies the problem! Smokers can't get a smoking room so they accept the non-smoking room, disable the smoke alarm, and puff away. This is a case of unintentional consequences of a well-meaning policy. The hotel should probably revert back to providing some smoking rooms.Anyways, I was given a new room and it was beautiful and even had a view (unlike my original one). It was clean, roomy, quiet, very comfortable bed, and had an excellent bathroom. The staff was very professional and friendly. One example was the doorman who shook my hand every time I entered the hotel. The concierge was top notch.The hotel has probably the best location of any hotel in N.O. - away from the craziness of the French Quarter and Canal St. yet close enough for an easy walk there. It's also an easy walk in the other direction to a number of fine museums. (I highly recommend the D-Day museum.)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great stay with our two-year-old at Le Pavillon With our two-year-old son, we recently took the train from Washington, DC to New Orleans and stayed at Le Pavillon. The hotel was wonderful. First of all, it's very centrally located in a nice area. We didn't rent a car, so we walked everywhere very easily. It's even just a 15-minute walk from the train station, so we never needed to bring a car seat. My husband strolled our son to the hotel while I took a taxi with our luggage. Our son got a fever the first day, and we called the concierge to get the name of a children's clinic. The concierge gave us the name of a clinic, along with the name and number of the hotel's house doctor. Their house doctor came to our room and checked out our son. What a luxury it was to have a doctor come to us, especially in an unfamiliar city! The room service staff was always friendly and prompt. Our son likes warm milk, and when we called to order it, the staff took extra steps to ensure that the milk arrived at our room at the right temperature! The restaurant staff went out of their way to make our meals there comfortable, as did all the staff. One day, our son was crying in the restaurant, so we strolled him around the lobby. We returned to the restaurant when, all of a sudden, a staff member who saw us in the lobby appeared with a big, blue balloon! We immediately had a happy, smiling child! Every night around 10 p.m., the hotel has a tradition of serving peanut butter and jelly sandwiches. It's beautifully done on silver platters, with various kinds of bread, jellies, peanut butter, hot chocolate, milk, coffee, etc. It's a fun thing to look forward to in the evening! We highly recommend Le Pavillon!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wowed by La Pavillon WOW was about the only thing my wife could say as we entered the lobby of La Pavillon Hotel. My wife and I were in New Orleans only for the night since we were leaving on a 5 day Carribean cruise the next afternoon. As we entered we were greeted by the doorman, a extremely polite young man, that remembered our names every time we saw him. Upon check-in we were informed our standard room was being upgraded at no extra charge to a suite. Again my wife was WOWed by the generousity of the Hotel. As the Bellman took our luggage and escorted us up to the 7th floor he gave us a nice overview of the history and layout of the Hotel. During the elevator ride up he asked us if we were on our honeymoon which we answered no but maybe you could count it as a second honeymoon because of the cruise. He said our suite is usually referred to as the Honeymoon Suite. As we came to the end of the hallway with my wife continually scanning the doors to find our room she realized the large set of french doors at the end were actually the entry into our suite, the Napoleon Suite. The word suite does not do justice to majesty and expansive this mini-apartment has to offer. The suite has its own foyer, sitting area w/fireplace, huge king size canopy bed w/curtains, magnificent bath area.I highly suggest and encourage everyone to stay at this beautiful hotel. The people enhance the feel and quality of your stay even as much as the hotel itself. We'll stay here everytime we come to New Orleans. Do yourself a favor and go to the La Pavillon website and see for yourself ther majesty and beauty of this gorgeous hotel.

<Content>Two thumbs up! We stayed at Le Pavillon in April 2005 and loved it. It is a beautiful hotel both inside and out. The pool/hot tub area on the roof is especially nice. The pbj at night was fun--don't miss it if you stay there. All of the staff was friendly and pleasant. It is about a 10 minute walk to the French Quarter and a short cab ride to the port (we went on a cruise). We would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>vegasblk
<Content>new orleans truth Spent 1 night in new orleans may 15-16, 2005. When you stay in or around the French Quarter/CBD, you know what to expect: high prices, one-way streets, cajun food, street performers, and lots of places to spend your money. This hotel is rated as #2 here and although it's a nice place in a nice location (street over from Canal St.), it does not deserve this high of a ranking. Why? The hotel has a 19th-century feel and building to match. For 99$/night I would have preferred the luxury of say the W hotel right down the street. We really didnt stay in the hotel very much except to sleep and did not explore it at all, but pictures can lie folks. Parking at the hotel was the standard $25/night, but there are plenty of cheaper parking garages close by. Harrah's casino, Emeril's and the Quarter are all very close. The room we had was small but clean. The lobby was big and pretty. Not the fabulous, plush, pleasure palace I expected but I didn't come for the hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>THE Place to Stay in New Orleans I stayed at the Hotel Pavillon while in New Orleans at a conference. I paid one hundred dollars a night less than my colleagues at the Hilton conference hotel, and they found themselves tremendously jealous. Le Pavillon is easily the most elegant, stunning hotel in which I have ever stayed. The opulence of the lobby, the friendliness and helpfulness of the staff, the splendor of the bar and restaurant, and the elegant layout and decoration of the rooftop pool all combined to make my experience at Le Pavillon fabulous. The room was beautiful, with high ceilings, tasteful decorations, and what my wife says is the most comfortable bed she has ever stayed in. For those in town for conferences, it is a six or seven minute walk to the river, five minutes to the French Quarter, and one block from the streetcar through the Garden District. I would highly recommend this hotel.

<Content>Fabulous hotel From the moment the doorman greeted us until the moment we checked out the service was exceptional. We were always welcomed with a smile - this is New Orleans, laissez les bon temps rouler! We were also upgraded to a large room upon our arrival at no extra cost - during Jazzfest no less!The lobby is grand and the rooftop pool is beautiful, lovely views at night. The PBJ service in the lobby is great, who doesn't love a little comfort food at the end of the day? It shocking to me how someone could criticize this hospitable touch, or think the staff was less than pleasant, but I suppose if you are looking for something to complain about, you can certainly find it!Our room was tastefully decorated, and the room service was efficient. Try the gumbo and banana bread pudding! Our cab driver recommended it as some of the best in the city and he was right! The housekeeping was great and we felt very taken care of. Our only concern was that we had a slow draining tub, not fun! But everything else was so above average, we didn't let something like that ruin our fun. We'll definitely be staying at Le Pavillon again!

After entering the hotel I was told in a rather rude manner that I would not be able to get into my room until 3pm. 3pm is a typical check-in time and I am fine with that, however the manner in which the clerk stated this to me was offensive.I went to lunch and returned at 2pm to find that a room was available so I checked in. I was told that I would be unable to obtain a key since the machine was not working and that the bellman would have to let me into my room.I found the room dark and musty, in fact an aerosol can sat next to the bed, along with miscellaneous cleaning supplies. There was a partially consumed bottle of soda in the fridge and the lock on the bathroom door was broken.After having an in-room spa treatment, I attempted to log onto the internet to find that the wireless signal was too weak to log onto, and the LAN connection was not working properly. I contacted the front desk who had an engineering clerk verify the problem. I was then transferred to another room.While packing my goods the clerk from the front desk rang to provide my new keys. No apology was provided and neither was a bellboy to help me transfer my luggage.The new room was not only smaller, but lacks the rain shower-head, has no handles on the shower doors, and the bed is terrible. The A/C filter was covered with dirt and falling from the ceiling.All in all my experience here in New Orleans has not been made pleasant by the Pavillon Hotel.

<Content>Highly Recommended My wife, 9 year old son  I enjoyed our week long stay. The lobby is beautiful and welcoming. All our room requests were honored. <Content>Loved Le Pavillon April 4, 2005: For the second time in the last four months I had to spend a day in New Orleans in conncection with an early morning appearance at the US Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals. The first time my 25 year old daughter accompanied me. This time my husband and 17 year old daughter accompanied me. Both times provided us all with wonderful experiences. The rooms were lovely with beautiful furnishings and everything in perfect working order. There were far too many little details for me to take time to mention here which made me feel so welcome and appreciated. I must mention one...the business cards with my name on them as a guest at the LePavillon. How easy to share with other counsel who were staying at other hotels! The meal in the Crystal Dining Room last December was most enjoyable. The room was so very quiet for me while my companions were out sightseeing around New Orleans. The internet hook-up was a nice surprise. All in all, Le Pavillon will be the first place I call if I head down to the Fifth Circuit again. It is a short walk there from a fantastic hotel where I can prepare and get a good night sleep. I highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Elegant, Friendly, Delicious...My Dream Home The experience started when we approached Le Pavillion. The red carpet and the gloved doorman in formal attire with top hat set the standard for our entire stay...friendly, competent service with style. The lobby, though very elegant, is a very comfortable place to sit and read. The front desk was knowledgable and efficient; so was the bellman who helped with our luggage when we arrived before check-in. We had the experience of having someone ring for our elevator, and our room was provided with the standard accomodations one would expect along with a few surprises. The decorative painting on the ceiling and lighted picture above the headboard were very comforting touches. The restroom received high marks for the packaging of toiletries and exceptionally high marks for the anti-steam fogging mirror. My husband found great comfort in the terry cloth robes provided. They make wonderful cover-ups when travelling to the rooftop pool and hot tub. The rooftop pool was truly breathtaking from the personal cabanas to elevated hot tub to heated pool overlooking the city. Even in February with a slight chill in the air, the pool was a must. The decorative ballustrades and stone lions didn't hurt my illusion that I was in a different country. We took advantage of the concignere service to locate and make reservations at superb restaurants.  The Peanut Butter and Jelly Chef--make it a priority in your schedule to take advantage of the evening snacks. The hot chocolate with very heavy and rich whipped cream cannot be on any Weight Watcher's list, but it was euphoric. The Chef truly made it an experience with his personality and friendliness. Whatever they are paying him needs to be increased. He personified my experience at Le Pavillion--friendly, professional, and unexpected fun. My only regret is that we did not take advantage of the turn down service as did others in our party. The report either defied description or he was just very inadequate with words. Do not listen to reports that you have to stay in the French Quarter. You are close enough to walk there or to the trolley (I felt safe walking at night), but I was far enough away to be able to get a good night's sleep and get away from the party atmosphere. The next time I return to New Orleans, I want to stay in Le Pavillion. Until then, I just look at the toiletry samples I stashed in my luggage and dream of better days when I was royalty.  
<Date>Apr 14, 2005

<Author>easw
<Content>Wonderful experience at the Le Pavillon My husband and I stayed at this marvelous hotel for four nights in early March. Valet parking in the lot next door was lighted and very safe. The bellboy and door man were efficient and friendly, as were all the staff we interacted with. At check-in my husband jokingly mentioned an upgrade, and to our surprise we were given one. Our deluxe queen/queen room on the 5th floor was small but the high ceilings made it feel larger. Lots of interesting details in the room--framed prints of local plantations hung by gold cord on the walls, black granite countertops in the bathroom, a ceiling fan, plush curtains (that really blocked the morning daylight), lots of decorative pillows piled on each bed and a doorbell outside each door on this floor. Other amenities were also impressive. The 32-inch TV in the armoire was unexpected. The bathroom, while small, was nicely done with plenty of towels and a heater fan to warm the chill. The closet had plenty of room, as well as a fair-sized safe. The beds were moderately firm and comfortable, with double-sheeted blankets. The gym on the top floor had the customary endurance machines as well as weight training. The fridge there was stocked with Powerade and water, and there was a large basket with complimentary apples and bananas on top of the fridge. The rooftop pool area overlooking the city was very nice, with a small heated pool, hot tub and cabanas. We did not eat in the restaurant while we were there, but we did order room service for breakfast one morning. My eggs benedict was found to have quite a bit of egg shells in one half, but this replaced quickly after one call to dining, and the new dish was excellent. We did the PBJ one night, and thought it fun and quirky. Turn down service was prompt and included a complimentary PBJ cookie and bottle of water.Although the hotel decor (especially the lobby) is very ornate, we never felt out of place on those days we were wearing casual clothes. The hotel is withing walking distance to the French Quarter (Bourbon Street is three blocks away) and a bit more of a hike to Riverwalk and other nearby attractions. There is a Garden District streetcar stop a block-and-a-half away.Our receipt at check-out reflected accurate charges and was a great deal (special internet rates), considering all the amenities we enjoyed. We would not hesitate to stay at Le Pavillon again.  
<Date>Mar 24, 2005

<Author>gazza53
<Content>OK but nothing special Stayed at Le Pavillon for 4 days in early Feb 2005. I had expected great things but have to say the experience was generally disappointing from the minute I arrived. Although there were a number of bell staff around there was no offer of help with bags etc. Then had to play guess the window at reception - they were all too busy having a chat to check me in! The room itself was OK although extremely dark - it also had an unusual odour which was also noticeable along the corridor (I was on the 3rd floor). Breakfast was ok - but dinner was very disappointing (try Smith  Wollensky - 2 blocks up Poydras - a much better option). I met some business contacts and we tried to have a quiet drink in the bar - however this proved impossible as within minutes the entertainment began - consisting of a lady playing piano and singing very LOUDLY! I know New Orleans is famed for its music but could really have done without this. I also understand that the PBJ is a bit of a tradition but it seemed rather a waste of time and money to me- the only time I was actually in the Hotel at 10pm there were very few takers - most people still being out on the town (this is New Orleans after all!)Final straw was at check out where I was accused of having emptied the mini bar of snacks and candies - which I hadn't actually touched . Nevertheless took some persuasion to get it taken off the bill. Overall the hotel's supposed belle epoch character didn't gell with the reality of staying there - it was ok but for the money I'll try soemwhere else next time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place to stay I stayed at this lovely hotel in August of 2003 and it was great, my favorite place to stay in NOLA. Nice quiet location but only a short walk to the French Quarter. There is also a street car stop very close by. Perhaps one of the best things about this hotel though is that starting around 6pm on Friday until Monday morning, there is an abundance of free and safe parking on the street behind/beside the hotel. We could see our vehicle from our hotel room and it was perfectly safe all weekend...for FREE, no $15 - 25 a night fee. The staff was also great (was a staff member who let us know about the great free parking!) and the room while on the small side was extremely cozy and quite lux with a nice padded armchair and beautiful furniture (even decorative throw pillows for the bed). New Orleans is my favorite weekend getaway spot, I get there at least once a year and Le Pavillon is best place I've stayed.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel We just returned from our second stay that the Le Pavillon, and will definitely return again. The hotel is very impressive with lots of historical architecture and decor. The rooms are very comfortable and have high ceilings, marble bathrooms, and free high speed internet access. The location is convenient to most places in town. The staff is friendly and helpful. The breakfast in the restraunt was wonderful - try the bananas foster waffles! The pbj sandwiches in the evenings were also a welcome homecoming. My only caution is to be very careful with the mini-bar. It is computerized, and incorrectly charged us for items that moved when we opened the door. However, the staff handled it very well and gladly removed the charges. We have stayed in many hotels in New Orleans over the years, and Le Pavillon is our favorite so far.

<Author>larlar
<Content>JUST SO-SO Overall, I would have to say that our stay at Le Pavillon was rather disappointing. For a hotel of its standards, I was hoping for a grand and spectacular experience, but a few instances made it less than ordinary.Upon our arrival, there was no doorman to greet us, open the door and assist with our luggage. We were greeted in a tepid manner by the front desk. We were made to wear annoying, lime green bracelets that we had to keep on for four days (it reminded me of some wild college spring break when bracelets are handed out at bars for unlimited drinks). Our room was rather small; the space provided did not create the feeling of luxury that the hotel boasted. Our toiletries were crammed onto the sink. We wanted to have a small meal at the Gallery Lounge, and the waiter was very delayed in his service. We were seated, and we waited to place our order while the waiter ran around serving others. He completely forgot about us, especially when a busload of tourists arrived to order drinks at the bar. It was obvious that he was not going to get around to taking our orders anytime soon, so we left our table completely disturbed by the experience, and we could not help but let it negatively affect our perception of the hotel--where was the hospitality that Le Pavillon boasted of?????? AND, he had the nerve to look annoyed when he finally noticed us leaving our table. Also, I was inquiring about the times when luncheon was being served at the front desk, and the woman was very brusque about her response, and once again I felt completely put off by the lack of hospitality. Housekeeping was not very thorough in cleaning the rooms--I found an apple core underneath the bed that housekeeping had failed to clean up!Two factors do stand out with regards to a more positive experience at this hotel--the late night snack hour and the turn down service. The chef was very open and friendly, and the late night snacks a delight. The nightly turn down service was very charming and gave me the feel of luxury. However, with the aforementioned negative events, I will not be returning to this hotel for another stay.

<Author>Seb_In_Kansas
<Content>A great hotel for a good time in New Orleans Hi,We stayed 4 nigths in the Pavillon Hotel fron Jan 5 to 9, 2005.This hotel is really nice, it is an Historic Hotel. Once you enter this Hotel you know you are going to be pampered there. The service was great, from minute one everybody was very helpful. The decor was really nice (painted ceilling in the bedroom, Grand Chandelier in the loby, mirror and gold everywhere, Marble in the bathrooms). One little thing is: we had a room with a king bed and the room was just a bit small for this size bed, but we still had room to move around. The room was very quiet, we never heard anything from the surrounding rooms (even if they were occupied) or the street (we were on the 3rd floor).We ate at the Crystal room (the hotel restaurant) for breakfast and had their special buffet. The food was very tasty and I wiil advise you to try their Bananas Foster Waffles.We enjoyed their roof top Heated pool and Hot tub everyday. Even the decor around these area was great (statues, gas lamp at nigth). We did not use their gym, but we checked it ou, it look very well equiped and with good quality cardio machines and lot of free weigths. They offer water, Gatorade, towel at the gym it was surrounded with windows on the roof of the hotel, there were a good ligth in it. We also loved the free HIGH SPEED INTERNET and the snack of hot chocolate, peanut butter and jelly snadwiches, fruits, milk, orange juice, cookies they have available at 10:00 pm.The location of the hotel is great, in between the French Quarter (5-10 minutes walk) and the garden district, only one block from St Charles trolley line and two blocks from Canal street trolley line. It is a great location to discover what New Orleans has to offer. We also felt secure walking in the area even at nigth. There is also all around the hotel plenty of nice restaurants, like Herbsaint (my Favorite).We'll go back there on my next trip to New Orleans. We choose this hotel in the first place because their rates for what they offer were great, we'll come back there just for their service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't listen to the negative reviews! I can't believe that this hotel had any bad reviews! Our stay was great and well worth the price! Our reservations were quickly handled over the phone and the hotel promptly honored their lowest price guarantee. Upon check-in the staff was friendly and professional. They were able to answer all of our questions and offer pertinent information about NO. The bell staff was great! They were friendly, jovial and prompt. The room was beautiful. I had heard that their rooms were small however I did not find this to be the case. Their standard room is between 350-450 square feet. If this is not large enough for you they have a deluxe room that is 500 square feet as well as the junior suite and suite, the largest being 1500 square feet. The counter top in the bathroom was a little small but this was not a problem 鈥?it might have been if I were planning to move in鈥?Oh, there is not a coffee maker in the room.Room service was also good and the prices were equivalent to those of any restaurant in NO. One thing you don鈥檛 need to miss is the peanut butter and jelly sandwiches! This was a lot of fun and the sandwiches were great. They are served between 10pm and 11pm in the lobby of the hotel.Parking at the hotel is $25 per night. I thought this was a reasonable price considering their was an attendant in the lot 24/7 and this included valet parking (except tip).The only problem that I ran across was contacting the concierge before our arrival. I tried to contact the concierge for 7 days before I finally got a response by then I no longer needed their service as I had made the arrangements myself using outside catering services and floral shops. Next time I stay at the hotel, I will be more adamant about reaching the concierge. (Don鈥檛 bother leaving a message or emailing 鈥?stay on hold until they are forced to answer the phone.)I will definitely return to this hotel!Mary Lynne Williams

<Author>peace through travel
<Content>Historical I am a travel agent and got a good rate in sabre (no travel agent discount just a published rate of 129/night) The agency is a member of the Giants (Ensemble) consortium and I checked the Giants hotel book to see if this hotel was in it (this is usually an indicator of a superior hotel and offer added amenities)- it was. The procedure to set up the added amenities is given and a description of these amenities is on their website. The added amenities for the Le Pavillon for clients of Giants agencies is 'upgraded room, early check in, late check out and a fruit basket with a bottle of water'. I emailed the hotel a few days before arrival from home and told them that we would be celebrating our 25th anniversary. When we arrived we were upgraded to one of the rooms that had been recently renovated (I am unsure if they were renting the non-renovated rooms at all at that time). In our room was a card in the fruit basket saying 'congratulations on your 25th anniversary'. We asked to stay later on our departure as we had a late flight (we were told we would have to pay for a half day). When I asked reception about the Giants amenity, she said she had never heard of Giants. I asked her to ask Mr. Morin - he let us stay for free until 3:30. To make a long story short I was amazed that they had the audacity to imply that the upgraded room, and late check out were for our anniversary when they were contracted through Giants. The concierge was not friendly and would not permit my husband to take one of the magazines she had set out on the desk in front of her, saying 'you have one of those in your room'. When we got to the room we did not have one. The hallway became full of furniture on day two - a weird smell was about - were they fumigating? The location is good, the rooms are large, the city is wonderful. Would I stay again? No.

<Author>WineBuffinMN
<Content>La Pavillon is a GREAT place to stay! On a recent trip to New Orleans, my husband and I took the advice of many websites and decided to stay at Le Pavillon Hotel. It was a wonderful experience from start to finish!The staff consistently called us by name and were very very friendly; whether it was greeting us back to the hotel, setting up tours for us or helping us with directions around the city. Le Pavillon is a short walk to the French Quarter and the Central Business District--so you're close to some of the major sites. The hotel is very well kept and CLEAN; something that we very much appreciated since we were in the Big Easy. Our room was a standard, run of the mill one, but nonetheless, it was beautiful, just like the rest of the hotel.Le Pavillon has a nice exercise room with complimentary fruit and sports drinks, in addition to a relaxing pool and whirlpool on the roof of the hotel. They also serve peanut butter and jelly sandwiches, milk and fruit every night at 10:00PM--something that many of the guests took part in!I highly recommend La Pavillon Hotel as a place to stay if this is your first or 50th time to New Orleans. Without the staff at Le Pavillon, our trip wouldn't have been as fun!!

<Content>5 Star hotel! We thoroughly enjoyed our stay at the Le Pavillon in New Orleans during Thanksgiving week. First the bad things - we booked through the hotel and took advantage of their lowest rate guarantee (if you find their hotel cheaper on another site, they will give you a rate 10% less than the rate you found). We found a cheaper rate and emailed them, recieving a prompt response and an offer of 10% less than the rate we found. But when we arrived to check in, the front desk was uniformed of the rate change or the entire concept of the lowest rate guarantee. Not only ignorant, but RUDE!!! They acted as if we made this up to try and get a better rate unfairly, and did nothing to verify what we (THE CUSTOMERS ) were telling them. The standard double room has a tiny bathroom with no counter space for your toiletries, a useless hair dryer, and you have to ASK for a coffee machine (which didn't work well). The rooftop pool and spa area was admittedly beautiful but the spa was set at such a high tempeture (with no noticeable controls anywhere to be found) that it scalded us - we were literally bright red from our knees down , all that we could tolerate. All of the employees we encountered (other than those above) were friendly, helpful and knowledgeable. The room service late night snack we had after exploring Bourbon Street was HORRID!! The pizza was cardboard like and greasy, with an unpleasant taste. The deli sandwiches were just average. This was certainly not worth the $46 dollars we spent on a snack we didn't/couldn't finish. All in all, I think that my money would have been better spent elsewhere - this is not at all the first time I have visited New Orleans but the first time I felt compelled to write a review.  
<Date>Oct 4, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>An A+ hotel Just got back from Le Pavillon yesterday and have to truly admit it was the best hotel stay ever! The pool area was beautiful, nice and breezy, the jacuzzi was awesome and the cabana area was very relaxing. If anyone has any questions about this place, you may e-mail me and I'll be glad to answer. I highly recommend Le Pavillon and hopefully can stay again in the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>They try hard, but fall somewhat short Not a bad hotel, but the overall impression I get is of an establishment trying very hard to be posh and falling somewhat short. The decor is pleasant, but not perfectly maintained. The housekeeping was questionable - I had to hunt for certain articles that would disappear under the bed during cleaning and, during one of these hunting expeditions, found a strange pair of women's underwear! Turndown service varies from night to night, and was missed altogether on certain nights. The walls are thin and sounds from the hallway can be instrusive. Do ask for one of the renovated rooms - the bathrooms are much nicer. Calls are expensive, local or otherwise. Overall it was a pleasant stay, it was just lacking in some of the features associated with hotels of the calibre it is striving for.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Cool Gas Lamp, Beautiful Lobby, nice room, though a little small I stayed for two nights last Summer with my wife and nephew. I was really impressed by the lobby, which is on par with the Peabody in Memphis, though smaller. It was very much in the same vein of an older, fancy (though not super-luxury) hotel. The lobby had a nice Frenchy-New Orleans look. The rooms were kind of small, but not as bad as the Peabody. The decor in the rooms was not on par with the lobby, though that is true of most hotels. If you are looking for a charming room in New Orleans for about the same price, I would recommend the Josephine Guest House in the Garden District. My nephew really was looking forward to the peanut butter and jelly buffet in the lobby, so we went and enjoyed it very much.It is a bit of a walk to the French Quarter, which I was a bit wary of at first. With the tighter policing in New Orleans recently, I felt safe. I would not have stayed there a few years ago though, especially with children.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Old World Charm and old fashioned service prevail here! Not fond of flying, and especially amidst the raising of terrorism alert to orange, I didn't sleep x-mas eve; I was set to fly to New Orleans on Christmas Day 2003 and bound for Le Pavillon Hotel. Check-in was painless and courteous, which was great since I hadn't slept a wink the night before and had a migraine to boot from the tension. As soon as I checked into the room I was rewarded by cleanliness and old world charm. I even took pictures of the ceilings, which sported crown moldings and hand-painted flowers! Within minutes of checking in I relaxed to the point of having my migraine vanish. I had made reservations for x-mas dinner that evening at the restaurant inside the hotel.The only glitch was when I showed up at the restaurant and they didn't have my name down for the reservation, even though I had confirmed it upon arrival. Despite this, Christmas Dinner was spectacular. Also, the hotel didn't have a shuttle (free or otherwise) to the French Quarter. However, that was fine with me since I didn't enjoy the drinking scene so much. Even though I left generous tips daily for the maid service, they got chintzy with the bath products after my second day. Also, my room was right up against the stairwell, not a good idea if you don't want to hear the staff鈥檚 early morning hall traffic. That鈥檚 IT for complaints.I don't stay at a hotel anymore without checking out reviews at www.tripadvisor.com. Only Le Pavillon was one of the few with so many (well-deserved) positive reviews. That's the main reason I stayed there. I felt perfectly safe there and in the surrounding neighborhood, which I often walked around, as far as The French Quarter. The walk is great because you get to experience the little artsy shops along the way. Right around the corner of hotel I found a little convenience store and a Subway. There is also a lovely casino about 10 blocks away.Two charming points of the hotel were: the peanut butter and jelly sandwiches with hot cocoa in the lobby every evening. However, somewhere on the internet site it said it was at midnight. It was more like at 10:00 p.m. (can't remember now). One late night I came in from the cold to the welcoming, warm, and beautifully decorated x-mas lobby with this little feast laid out so beautifully. Charming!!! To boot, this little soir茅e was free and it also provided an opportunity to meet fellow guests (met some cool people there). Another charming, albeit strange claim to fame of this hotel (for you sensitives out there) is that the hotel is one of the most haunted in New Orleans. Trust me, it was, but nothing scary, just another aspect of its charm!The bonus of my trip (thanks to the shuttle driver from the airport) was the Egyptian traveling antiquities exhibition at the New Orleans Museum of Art (www.noma.org) called The Quest for Immortality. It ended Feb. 2004, but this museum is well worth exploring, they have a rich and diversified collection from all over the world. This was the highlight of my trip. Don't worry, I did manage to get a drink in at the oldest bar, LaFitte鈥檚 (sp?) Blacksmith's Shop the day of departure.I was happily surprised with the turndown service. The room was cleaned, bed turned down with two generous, delectable cookies, soft music, and a dimmed spotlight bathing the painting above the bed, a relaxing prelude to a good night's sleep. My stay here was great and I would do it again in a heartbeat. Highly recommend to the woman traveling alone.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not an ordinary hotel! From the second my husband and I arrived at Le Pavillon we knew that we were in for an incredible stay in New Orleans! The staff was outstanding and extremely helpful! The rooms had a warm cozy feel to them and the rooftop swimming pool was also an extra treat. We were visiting for my husbands birthday, so we asked the concierge Justin for a recommendation for a restaurant. He made reservations for us, and after we left, he called the restaurant back to tell them that it was his birthday. On arrival, they had complimentary champagne waiting! It was magnificent! The hotel is also in an excellent location. Easy access to the streetcars and buses, and it is also an easy walk to the river and Bourbon street. I have recommended this hotel to all my family and friends and I will continue to recommend it to anybody travelling to New Orleans. I know on my visit back I will again choose Le Pavillon!  
<Date>Apr 3, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best **** hotel in the world with the best staff!! I read reviews on tripadvisor.com for months prior to our 4th anniversary excursion to New Orleans. I'm never been more confident about referring a hotel to anyone! Stay here, you won't be sorry!!

<Content>Le Pavillon - "Le Excellent" My brother  I had to make a last minute trip to New Orleans because our 94 year old Nana was in the Cardiac Care ward of Ocshners Hospital.My experience at Le Pavillon began at the front door when I was greeted like an old friend instead of just another hotel visitor. The staff at Le Pavillon were very coridal and professional when they thought we were on holiday, and went even above and beyond when they knew our visit held potential for great sadness.Two of my three favorite people I never even met face to face. The ladies answering the phone in Room Service. Amazing. I spend most of my time in hotels in South East Asia and other parts of the world, so I can tell you these ladies were fabulous. The food was served in the time frame they stated, and was wonderful. From oatmeal to their house specialty beouf bourguignon, I recommend it all.Our other favorite was their very talented singer/piano player. What an incredible voice, and a personality to draw you out of any sadness.The entire staff shouldn't be forgotten, everything was imaculate and so much southern charm!I must admit, my brother and I really got a kick out of the Peanut Butter  Jelly Sandwich bar with Hot Chocolate at night. We had never heard of such thing, but what a crowd pleaser. Imagine standing in an elegant lobby with everyone gathering between 10pm - 11pm making PBJ sandwiches... my brother of course, put too much jelly on his and spilled all over the nice carpet... even in our mid 40's he is still a little boy.SO, book a stay at the hotel and enjoy the experience, the rooms were nice  the beds comfortable. My brother  I look forward to going back for a happy occassion and taking our spouses for the experience!

<Author>dananyc
<Content>Fabulous but be cautious.. My husband and I just came back from a fantastic stay at Le Pavillon. We chose this hotel because of all the great reviews and were so happy we did. If you've read some of them, you know all the good stuff (it's true!) already. I just wanted to let you know that there was a guest walking back to the hotel last week who was killed for no reason (he was right across the street). It was only 10:30 at night and nobody knows why. I DO encourage you to stay here, but DEFINITELY take taxis after dark as New Orleans is very sketchy. Even if you are only going a few blocks away, it is worth the four or five bucks. Keep in mind that Le Pavillon is in the business district so the streets are pretty empty after 6pm. We live in NYC and feel much safer here than in NO. Having said that, we felt the hotel was first class in every way and the staff was very helpful and offered great recommendations. We will be back!  
<Date>Dec 31, 2003

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Amazing Hotel, Why do people complain? As a Hotel School student in Lausanne, I was amazingly pleased to have had the opportunity to stay in such a grandiose hotel for over 2 weeks. Before going any further I wanted to share what I have learned here in my Hotel School In Lausanne: Types of Complainers Passives: no complaint, no negative wom, no third-party action Voicers: actively compain but less likely to negative wom (i.e. service providers best friend) Irates: negative wom, likely to switch (feel alienated from the marketplace) Activists: above average propensitiy to complain on all dimensionsWhat Customers expect when they complain: fair treatment Outcome fairness: customers expect ompensation that would match the level of their dissatisfaction, punishment should fit the crime (e.g. money, apology, future free service) Procedural fairness: in terms of policies, rules and timeliness of the complaint process Interaction fairness: expect to be treated politely and honestly People voicing their thoughts on this site are of course activists such as I am and really do want to be heard. When faced with problems in the hotel (which happened very occasionally) such as down-service slightly delayed during high occupancy periods, or a room service meal arriving slightly colder than expected or a problem with the contents, they were always ready to offer complimentary delights. Fair treatment, mixed with great respect and breathtaking service is what you can expect from such a hotel. Thank you le Pavillon for all you have to offer.  
<Date>Dec 2, 2003

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolute Elegance I loved my stay at Le Pavillon! The lobby was beautiful and I found the staff to be most helpful, right down to the man at the door who not only opened the door for me, but also took my hand to help me up and down the steps! The roof top pool and hot tub were also beautiful with fountains and statues and extra towels so you don't have to use the ones from your room. Our room was very nice with mattresses and pillows that were more comfortable than any hotel I've ever stayed in and almost more comfortable than my own bed at home! The towels were thicker than any hotel towel I've ever used and the bathrobes were another nice bonus. Little details like this is what made my stay at Le Pavillon so wonderful. The peanut butter and jelly sandwiches and hot chocolate at night were the perfect before bed snack. While my stay would have been far too expensive for me without my conference discount and sharing a room with 3 other people, I would still find a way to stay here again. The people at the front desk were very nice about taking off parking charges for 3 days that we were not parked in their lot. No arguments at all! I would recommend this hotel to anyone traveling to New Orleans!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Real Dowager Queen of New Orleans Over the years, I have probably visited New Orleans eight or ten times. I normally enjoy my stay, and my overall experience with hotels there has been about average.This trip, a colleague suggested the Le Pavillon Hotel, which she touted as being a necessary part of experiencing the a real New Orleans hotel - not just a another cookie-cutter, look-alike, chain hotel property.She was absolutely correct.From the moment you approach the entrance door, you are treated with respect and kindness by a staff who actually make you feel welcomed and comfortable; without that forced, plastic smile that you know comes out of a standard hotel employee training course entitled Whatever Happens,SMILE!The main lobby is warm, elegant and comfortable. The lobby bar is inviting and intimate. The hotel restaurant (I am sorry to say I have forgotten its name) is an absolute gem! It is the antithesis of everythinh I have come to expect from a hotel restaurant. The room itself has an authentic New Orleans decor and ambiance; but do not let that fool you into thinking that that is all it has. The decor, staff, service and menu are truly world-class.Although this is an old property, the facilities are completely modernized, and it is clear that renovation of the physical plant is an important constant part of management's mindset. The room I had was elegantly appointed and comfortably designed and furnished. The public spaces of the hotel are very well maintained.The next time you go to New Orleans, try something different. Stay three or four blocks outside of the French Quarter (but within the Business District), and treat yourself to experiencing a stay at what I would call the Dowager Queen of New Orleans.  
<Date>Oct 9, 2003

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We felt like Royalty at Le Pavillion We stayed one memorable night in New Orleans on our way to Pensacola Beach. Le Pavillion was gorgous! Doormen, Bellman, conceirge, outstanding decor..... Our room was one with bay windows. There was a raised, decorated ceiling with a ceiling fan. The beds were covered with beautiful decorative pillows. The furnishings, linens and room decor were quite fancy. The bathroom was unbelievable! Wonderful shower, beautiful sink, and black tile floors. They even provide comfortable bath robes to use in the room. My children were extremely impressed! We all went for a midnight swim in the rooftop pool. It was an experience I think my kids will always remember fondly. We walked to the French Quarter. It is not far and we never felt threatened, but it may be safer to take a taxi. Our children are 3, 10 and 13. Valet parking is required and I believe it cost $25 per night. It is billed directly to the room. Most, if not all hotels in the French quarter area charge for parking. The cheapest hotel parking we saw was $10. We got the beautiful room at Le Pavillion for such a great price that we could afford to park too. Note: I recommend you have your own sodas, etc. They are quite pricey at the hotel. **We found that there is complementary bottled water, sport drinks, and fruit in the workout room. We would definately stay there again if we could get the room for such a good deal.

<Content>A gracious, genteel southern hotel La Pavillon is truly and extraordinary hotel, a step back in time. From the moment of your arrival, you will feel the warmth and graciousness that is the hallmark of this establishment, as if you are their most honored guest.The hotel itself is an architectural jewel that is a feast for the eyes. Many hotels have spectacular architecture, rare and exotic flowers, crystal and silver in abundance, and the finest in bedding, but it is the people who give any hotel its life. Le PaVillon is a treasure - one we hope is never lost.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel--check around first My sister and I booked the La Pavillon at the referral of two friends from New Orleans. We were pleased with the appearance of the hotel...and also the greeting  check-in upon arrival. Be aware that your options are limited with parking. You will pay almost the same amount whether you choose valet service or 'park your own'. Our room was very small, but clean. The 'extras' were nice... our beds turned down every evening, music playing and lights dimmed...peanut butter and jelly sandwiches for late night snack... Having the robes is a nice feature... But... you cannot purchase sodas, water, or snacks at this hotel---except from the unbelievably over-priced mini-bar. A Diet Coke cost me $5.29. But with no refrigerator  no vending machines---you have no other choice if you need to have a drink of some sort... Breakfast at the restaurant was delicious but overpriced... Overall, we enjoyed our stay at the hotel. The next time we return to New Orleans, though, I believe we will stay at a hotel located within the French Quarter or very close by...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>So disappointed. After two weeks of careful planning for our trip to New Orleans, we were counting on a two night stay at La Pavillon to kick it off in grand style. The minute we walked into the lobby I knew we were in trouble. It was dirty, smelled of smoke and stale food and in desperate need of touch-up paint all over. We had to wait 35 minutes to check in due the the lack of organization at the front desk. Things only got worse when shown to our room. It, too, smelled of smoke (we don't smoke), the carpet was torn and dirty, the bathroom had mold in the grout, the bathtub was stained, and the room needed paint. The basic feel to everything was shabby and dirty. Yuk. We did ask to see another room, and it was no cleaner or better. We actually stayed only one night of our planned two because we were so repulsed. I also accidentally left my pillow in the room, and they have me jumping through hoops to try and get it back. Lots of promises, no action. We left the room 30 minutes after checking in and walked two blocks down the the Monaco hotel and reserved a room for the next night. Stay there! It's EVERYTHING we wanted - clean, cool, fun and lots of additional perks.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Le Pavillon is first class What a lovely hotel! This is an older hotel that's been kept up beautifully, from the lovely paintings to the marble floors and french antiques. The staff of a hotel can make or break your stay, and the folks here definately did their very best to ensure that our stay was the best ever. Requests for service were completed quickly and effortlessly. The concierge helped us with everything from a no-hassle, one-day car rental to restaurant suggestions and tour information. The restaurant is excellent (and the peanut butter and jelly sandwiches in the lobby every night aren't bad either!). Nice, safe location - you will probably want to take a cab to the quarter, but they are very inexpensive (about $5) and always available. Very gracious, very elegant, very friendly. We'll definately be back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful but definite problems The hotel was beautiful and the bellman was wonderfully helpful and friendly. The night snacks in the lobby were very enjoyed by our children. Sadly, however, my husband had his wallet stolen by housekeeping at the pool. The wallet was returned, minus a substantial amount of money. My daughters toy was picked up by valet at night. We were told to pick it up in the morning, but it was missing by that time. My digital camera left our room. Our room service was delivered after the requested time frame. They did leave a bottle of wine as an apology. Nothing was ever done to compensate for our other problems at the hotel. My husband regulary stays at the Windsor Court. We have stayed there as a family several times. Any problems there are promptly taken care of courtesy of the hotel with profuse apologies. That is where we will be returning. If you choose to stay at La Pavillion, please be sure to behave as if you are on Bourbon Street with a pickpocket on you tail.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>As Good As it Gets!! If you're looking for luxury and special treatment and remarkably PERSONAL service, then Le Pavillon really is as far as you need to go. And no further. The first thing that you'll notice about Le Pavillon is that it's beautiful; those high ceilings, massive chandeliers, antique furniture and beautiful bannisters will strike you immediately. The next thing you'll notice, and the last thing that you'll forget, is that all of the people working there seem to think that this is a small hotel with a few guests - how they've managed to treat everyone with such warmth while still keeping things running smoothly in such a large hotel is a mystery to me.We had a fantastic time, the food was great, the room was lovely, the value was good and the service was outstanding. We'll definitely be staying here the next time we're in New Orleans.

While I was at Le Pavillon I did not even fell like I was at a hotel based on the treatment I received. It is rare in today's world to find a Hotel quite like this one. If you are doing New Orleans, do it right and stay a Le Pavillon, you definatly will remember it - I know I will for a long time to come!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Le Pavillon is Wonderful! My husband and I stayed at Le Pavillon for our honeymoon in early April, 2003. We stumbled across it on the Internet and, having stayed in New Orleans hotels before, were apprehensive about what we would find when we arrived. We should not have worried -- Le Pavillon is a beautiful and gracious hotel; the staff, from the concierge to the desk clerks, to the wait staff in the restaurant, to the doorman, were exceedingly helpful and friendly, above and beyond the call of duty. As guests in their hotel, they made us feel very welcome and very special. We were upgraded to a junior suite; our room was large, clean, and beautifully appointed. The amenities were first class, including fluffy white robes. This is a classy hotel with an attentive staff, and I would definitely stay at Le Pavillon again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Value was skin-deep We arrived and checked in on Ash Wednesday, the day after the end of Mardi Gras. The glitter and plush were as advertised. Doormen's service was average, check-in backed up badly and with only 1 active front-desk employee handling everyone. We got room 724 - I recommend against it. Queen bed and other furniture over-filled it. Very limited bureau storage, made much worse by the fact that in that room you can't open the bureau part of the combo tv-minibar-bureau unit enough to get its drawers open. We used our suitcases and the shelf in the closet, which is what we expect to do in an Econolodge (and often don't have to). Housekeeping was poor. We discovered a wine glass had been shattered near the window before we checked in, not cleaned up. Called about it at about 2 in the afternoon, it got cleaned up the next morning. A peanut on the floor in the bathroom never got picked up across 3 days. Soap not replaced, shower mat not replaced one day, etc. Minibar protected by infrared sensor that charges you for anything removed, made using it for personal medicine, etc., impossible. (If personal things get left in a minibara, that's certainly another housekeeping fault.) Phone charges are high ($1 for any call, plus time charges), shower head is the gentle rain style which was more of a drizzle, hot water only lukewarm one day, never very hot. Health and pool areas are nice, location was fine for us - we didn't mind the 5-minute walk to Canal St. Overall, overpriced for the value, is my opinion, along with patently uneven quality.  
<Date>Mar 14, 2003
